{"content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>More than 100 members of the European parliament have signed a letter of support for two whistleblowers convicted by a <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/luxembourg\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Luxembourg</a> court of leaking information about secret tax rulings to journalists.</p>\n<p>Antoine Deltour and Rapha\u00ebl Halet were both <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jun/29/luxleaks-pwc-antoine-deltour-avoids-jail-but-is-convicted-of-theft\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">convicted of theft earlier this year</a> after providing journalists with evidence that the rulings had helped multinational corporations slash their corporation tax bills to 1% or less. </p>\n<p>Revelations from the so-called LuxLeaks prompted demands for reform of the international tax system following their publication in 2014 by media organisations, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2014/nov/05/-sp-luxembourg-tax-files-tax-avoidance-industrial-scale\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">including the Guardian</a> and the International Consortium of Investigative Journalists. </p>\n<p>However, Luxembourg pursued criminal charges against Deltour and Halet with the support of their employer, the accountancy firm PwC, which had arranged the agreements. </p>\n<p>The MEPs used the letter to call for greater protection for whistleblowers at national and international level. \u201cWe can only but agree with judge Marc Thill who stressed in his deliberations that both of you should be considered as \u2018whistleblowers\u2019 and that the facts which you exposed are of crucial public interest by virtue of their contribution to a more transparent and fairer tax system,\u201d <a href=\"http://www.fabio-de-masi.de/kontext/controllers/document.php/215.9/d/1baa71.pdf\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">the letter reads</a>. </p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-1 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Labour plans radical overhaul at HMRC</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/sep/08/labour-radical-overhaul-hmrc-tax-avoidance\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>Tax rulings, also known as \u201ccomfort letters\u201d, are a practice whereby national tax authorities issue guidance to companies on how their corporation tax will be calculated. </p>\n<p>Although legal, the use of such rulings has become controversial following both the LuxLeaks reports and the revelation that <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/aug/30/apple-pay-back-taxes-eu-ruling-ireland-state-aid\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Ireland allowed Apple to reduce its corporation tax liability</a> for decades through its use of subsidiaries in the country. In 2014, the company paid a corporation tax rate of just 0.005%, according to Margrethe Vestager, the EU competition commissioner. </p>\n<p>Fabio De Masi, the German MEP who organised the letter and vice-president of a committee investigating <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/news/series/panama-papers\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">the Panama Papers,</a> criticised the Luxembourg authorities for also appealing against the acquittal of Edouard Perrin, a French investigative journalist accused of helping Halet. </p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s absolutely absurd that a journalist who covered Luxleaks is being brought to court,\u201d said De Masi. \u201cThis is a fundamental threat to press freedom. It\u2019s his job to cover these issues.\u201d </p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/sep/08/meps-support-convicted-luxleaks-whistleblowers-luxembourg", "summary": "Members call for greater legal protection for whistleblowers after conviction of ex-PwC workers over leaking of Luxembourg\u2019s secret tax rulings", "timestamp": "1473351996000", "author": "David Pegg", "title": "MEPs offer support to convicted LuxLeaks whistleblowers"}
{"content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>An American freelance journalist has been arrested in <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/turkey\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Turkey</a> after crossing the border from Syria, where she had been filming.</p>\n<p>Lindsey Snell was detained by Turkish authorities in early August and charged with \u201cviolating a military zone\u201d, according to a US state department spokesman <a href=\"http://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-37235315\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">who confirmed that she had been detained</a>.</p>\n<p>In <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/lindseysnel\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">a Facebook posting dated 5 August</a>, Snell related how she had been abducted while working in Syria two weeks before, but had managed to excape from her cave prison. Her captors were an Islamist group, Jabhat al Nusra, formerly an affiliate of al-Qaida, <a href=\"http://bigstory.ap.org/article/2c42b6d9795549689307da2f69516e95/al-qaida-central-appears-ok-split-syrian-branch\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">but now known as the Levant Conquest Front</a>.</p>\n<p>Snell, who says she is a Muslim, then fled from <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/syria\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Syria</a> only to be arrested again, this time by Turkish security forces in the southern Hatay province. US consular officials visited her in prison on 26 August.</p>\n<p>She is from Daytona, Florida, but has had a residency permit in Istanbul for the past 18 months where she rents an apartment, according to her husband, Suliman Wardak.</p>\n<p>He <a href=\"https://www.cpj.org/2016/09/freelance-journalist-lindsey-snell-detained-in-tur.php\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">told the Committee to Protect Journalists</a> (CPJ) he was detained for two days after security forces searched his wife\u2019s apartment on 22 August and confiscated her computer, video camera and other electronic equipment.</p>\n<p>The CPJ has demanded that the Turkish authorities release Snell. Its Europe and central Asia programme coordinator, Nina Ognianova, also said: \u201cWe call on the government to end its harassment of reporters crossing the border from Syria.\u201d</p>\n<p><em>Sources:</em> <a href=\"http://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-37235315\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">BBC</a>/<a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/lindseysnel\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Facebook</a>/<a href=\"http://bigstory.ap.org/article/2c42b6d9795549689307da2f69516e95/al-qaida-central-appears-ok-split-syrian-branch\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Associated Press</a>/<a href=\"https://www.cpj.org/2016/09/freelance-journalist-lindsey-snell-detained-in-tur.php\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">CPJ</a></p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/media/greenslade/2016/sep/02/american-journalist-detained-in-turkey-for-violating-a-military-zone", "summary": "After escaping from the clutches of an Islamist group in Syria, she was arrested after crossing the Turkish border", "timestamp": "1472814178000", "author": "Roy Greenslade", "title": "American journalist detained in Turkey for 'violating a military zone'"}

So journalists, like the rest of the public, were forced to buy tickets to obtain entry.</p>\n<p>But, despite buying a ticket, the Washington Post\u2019s correspondent, Jose DelReal, was refused entry to <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/the-fix/wp/2016/07/28/a-washington-post-reporter-was-banned-from-a-trump-pence-rally-yesterday-that-should-frighten-you/?campaign_id=A100&amp;campaign_type=Email#comments\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">a Milwaukee event on Wednesday night</a> featuring Trump\u2019s running mate, Mike Pence.</p>\n<p>He was stopped by an official who told him he couldn\u2019t enter the building with his laptop and cellphone. When he protested, a private security guard summoned the police and DelReal was patted down by two sheriff\u2019s deputies.</p>\n<p>According to a Huffington Post report on the matter, <a href=\"http://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/donald-trump-media_us_579a225ee4b02d5d5ed4a1cb?section\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Donald Trump\u2019s restrictions on the press including Politico, BuzzFeed, the Daily Beast, Univision and the <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/media/huffington-post\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Huffington Post</a>, are also on that list.</p>\n<p>Journalists are also upset about their movements being restricted at Trump campaign events, decisions which have even been enforced by the Secret Service. </p>\n<p>Pence\u2019s press secretary, Marc Lotter, later told the Post that campaign volunteers had misinterpreted the campaign\u2019s policy and that \u201cour events are open to everyone.\u201d</p>\n<p>But a Politco reporter who attended a rally with a general admission ticket last month was ordered out of the event while working on a laptop.</p>\n<p>Steven Ginsberg, the Post\u2019s senior editor for politics, told the HuffPost: \u201cWe will continue to cover their campaign in the same aggressive, comprehensive and unflinching way we have for the past 18 months, no matter what form their ban takes on any given day.\u201d </p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "url": {"content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/barack-obama\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Barack Obama</a> held \u201ccandid\u201d talks with Chinese president Xi Jinping on the knottiest disputes between the nations, the White House said on Saturday, as the president\u2019s final trip to Asia began with a difficult altercation between diplomats at the airport.</p>\n<p>The talks ranged across the most sensitive issues between the world\u2019s two largest economies: China\u2019s aggressive claims in the South <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/china\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">China</a> Sea, hacking and cybersecurity, and human rights and religious freedom, among others.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-1 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Breakthrough as US and China agree to ratify Paris climate deal</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2016/sep/03/breakthrough-us-china-agree-ratify-paris-climate-change-deal\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>Obama urged Xi to abide by the ruling of an international court against China\u2019s claims in the sea \u2013 a ruling that Beijing <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jul/12/philippines-wins-south-china-sea-case-against-china\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">promptly rejected</a> in July. The Hague ruled in favor of claims by the Philippines over the territory, where China has been expanding its military and <a href=\"http://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2015/07/30/world/asia/what-china-has-been-building-in-the-south-china-sea.html\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">building islands</a>.</p>\n<p>They also spoke about cybersecurity, and Obama similarly asked Xi to fulfill his obligations in a bilateral deal to protect against hacking between the nations. The discussion followed recent hacks pertaining to the US presidential election, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/technology/2016/jul/29/cozy-bear-fancy-bear-russia-hack-dnc\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">blamed on Russia</a>, and a national security hack last year,<a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/aug/10/chinese-national-security-officials-hack\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\"> allegedly conducted by Chinese operatives</a>.</p>\n<p>According to the White House, Xi and Obama agreed to implement a 2015 deal on cybersecurity and not \u201cconducting or knowingly supporting cyber-enabled theft of intellectual property for commercial gain\u201d \u2013 an issue that has <a href=\"https://www.donaldjtrump.com/positions/us-china-trade-reform\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">reached the campaign trail</a> in the US. They similarly discussed drug trafficking, and the White House praised new Chinese efforts against <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/apr/11/synthetic-opiates-drug-laws-w-18-fentanyl\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">the country\u2019s growing market of synthetic drugs</a>.</p>\n<p><strong> </strong>After the meeting, Obama described the talks in wary but respectful terms \u2013 a reflection of US-Chinese relations during his two terms \u2013 with many disagreements hanging between them.</p>\n<p>\u201cWhat I think we have been able to achieve is a practical and constructive effort where our interests intersect,\u201d he said. \u201cWe will have candid conversations about some of those differences, issues like human rights, or cyber or maritime. But our teams have been engaged they have worked very well and diligently together.\u201d</p>\n<p>The presidents spoke for over three hours and found accord on at least one issue: the 2015 global Paris climate deal, to which Obama and Xi <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2016/sep/03/breakthrough-us-china-agree-ratify-paris-climate-change-deal\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">formally committed the US and China</a> on Saturday. </p>\n<p>\u201cYes, diplomacy can be difficult and progress on the global stage can be slow,\u201d Obama said, before insisting that progress was possible. \u201cSome day we may see this as the moment when we decided to save our planet.\u201d </p>\n<p>The presidents also spoke about human rights and basic freedoms, and despite Obama\u2019s praise for American and Chinese diplomats, disagreements over one such freedom boiled over before talks even began. </p>\n<p>Members of the Chinese delegation objected angrily to the presence of American reporters \u2013 China has <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/media/greenslade/2016/jan/21/press-freedom-body-calls-for-eu-sanctions-against-chinese-media\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">broadly</a> <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/mar/08/chinese-magazine-challenges-government-censorship-organ\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">censored</a> the press <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/feb/12/china-journalism-reporters-freedom-of-speech\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">for years</a> \u2013 and as soon as the reporters who travel with Obama disembarked from Air Force One, one Chinese official began shouting demands to White House staff that American press be removed from the scene.</p>\n<p> A White House official defended the press\u2019 right to be there, and the Chinese official yelled back, \u201cThis is our country,\u201d according to the travelling press.</p>\n<p>The man then cast his ire at two of Obama\u2019s senior advisers, Ben Rhodes and Susan Rice, who only vaguely explained the spat to reporters: \u201cThey did things that weren\u2019t anticipated.\u201d Arguments continued through security into the Chinese state house, and one Chinese official helping the US delegation grew so angry that he began to shout at security and some of his colleagues. </p>\n<p>\u201cYou don\u2019t push people. No one gave you the right to touch or push anyone around,\u201d he yelled, according to the travelling press, who said that other American and Chinese officials soon intervened.</p>\n<p>\u201cStop, please,\u201d a foreign ministry official pleaded in Chinese. \u201cThere are reporters here.\u201d</p>\n<p>The dispute carried on even over how many reporters could watch the presidents go for a garden walk together. A Chinese official tried to limit press coverage, saying: \u201cThat is our arrangement.\u201d This prompted a White House official\u2019s retort: \u201cYour arrangement keeps changing.\u201d</p>\n<p>Most of the reporters were kept in a lobby, but two White House press members were eventually allowed to watch the leaders walk through a garden. \u201cI don\u2019t think the weather will be as good tomorrow as it is today,\u201d Xi said there, before changing the topic to tea.</p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/sep/03/barack-obama-xi-jinping-talks-hacking-south-china-sea", "summary": "White House releases statement after meeting on G20 sidelines, where US and China agree to ratify Paris climate deal", "timestamp": "1472928478000", "author": "Alan Yuhas", "title": "Wary Obama-Xi talks shadowed by diplomats' angry spat over press rights"}
{"content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>A court in Istanbul has remanded 17 Turkish journalists in custody as international concern mounts over the government\u2019s targeting of reporters.</p>\n<p>Twenty-one journalists appeared before a judge in hearings that lasted until midnight on Friday. Four were freed but 17 have been charged with membership of a terror group, the state-run Anadolu news agency said.</p>\n<p>Arrest warrants were issued this week for 89 journalists, at least 40 of whom have now been detained. The Turkish government has used a state of emergency law to order the closure of at least 131 newspapers, television and radio stations, publishers and news agencies.</p>\n<p>Some of those arrested used to work for the Zaman newspaper, which had close links with the Hizmet movement of the US-based Muslim cleric Fethullah G\u00fclen.</p>\n<p>The Turkish president, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/recep-tayyip-erdogan\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Recep Tayyip Erdo\u011fan</a> has accused G\u00fclen of helping to organise the coup. Zaman was taken over by government-appointed trustees in March and is now strongly pro-Erdo\u011fan.</p>\n<p>Mahir Zeynalov, a Washington-based correspondent for <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Today%27s_Zaman\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Today\u2019s Zaman</a>, the English language version of the newspaper, has tweeted a series of images of Turkish journalists being arrested on Friday.</p>\n<figure class=\"element element-tweet\" data-canonical-url=\"https://twitter.com/MahirZeynalov/status/758969729872637953\">\n<blockquote class=\"js-tweet tweet\">\n<img src=\"https://pbs.twimg.com/media/Cohm5S-UMAADiZ5.jpg\" alt=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"js-tweet-main-image tweet-main-image\"/>\n<span class=\"tweet-user\">\u2014 Mahir Zeynalov (@MahirZeynalov)</span>\n<a href=\"https://twitter.com/MahirZeynalov/status/758969729872637953\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"tweet-date\">July 29, 2016</a>\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\" class=\"tweet-body\">Nazli Ilicak, 72 years old veteran of Turkish journalism. He was later given a rapturous welcome by supporters.</p>\n<p>Emma Sinclair-Webb, the <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/turkey\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Turkey</a> director at Human Rights Watch, said: \u201cThe government crackdown is on media outlets and journalists it accuses of being linked to the Fethullah G\u00fclen movement, which it blames for the foiled military coup.</p>\n<p>\u201cIn the absence of any evidence of their role or participation in the violent attempt to overthrow the government, we strongly condemn this accelerated assault on the media, which further undermines Turkey\u2019s democratic credentials.\u201d</p>\n<p>Amnesty International also condemned the arrests. Its deputy Europe director, Fotis Filippou, said: \u201cRounding up journalists and shutting down media houses is the latest assault on a media already weakened by years of government repression ... the authorities are intent on silencing criticism without regard to international law.\u201d </p>\n<p>In a surprise move, Erdo\u011fan said late on Friday that he would drop all lawsuits brought against people for insulting him. The justice ministry said earlier this year that prosecutors had opened more than 1,800 cases against journalists, cartoonists and even children for insulting Erdo\u011fan since he became president in 2014.</p>\n<p>The move could be an attempt to silence his western critics, but it was not clear whether he would also abandon his legal action against the German comedian Jan B\u00f6hmermann, who recited a poem on German TV earlier this year suggesting that the Turkish leader engaged in bestiality and watched child pornography. </p>\n<p>The poem prompted Erdo\u011fan to file a complaint with German prosecutors that he had been insulted. Members of her own cabinet <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/apr/15/angela-merkel-agrees-prosecution-comedian-erdogan-poem\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">criticised the German chancellor, Angela Merkel, for acceding to the request</a> from Ankara to prosecute the comedian.</p>\n<p>In May, Boris Johnson, now the British foreign secretary, won a competition organised by the Spectator for <a href=\"http://www.theguardian.com/politics/2016/may/19/boris-johnson-wins-most-offensive-erdogan-poem-competition\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">writing a rude poem about Erdo\u011fan</a>. </p>\n<p>The limerick, published by the magazine as a rebuff to Erdo\u011fan\u2019s bid to prosecute the German comedian, jokingly implies that he has sex with a goat.</p>\n<p>Johnson, whose great-grandfather was Turkish, called it a scandal that a German court had granted an injunction to prevent B\u00f6hmermann repeating his skit.</p>\n<figure class=\"element element-tweet\" data-canonical-url=\"https://twitter.com/MahirZeynalov/status/758982032856748032\">\n<blockquote class=\"js-tweet tweet\" data-conversation=\"none\">\n<img src=\"https://pbs.twimg.com/media/CohyGHMVIAICFMc.jpg\" alt=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"js-tweet-main-image tweet-main-image\"/>\n<span class=\"tweet-user\">\u2014 Mahir Zeynalov (@MahirZeynalov)</span>\n<a href=\"https://twitter.com/MahirZeynalov/status/758982032856748032\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"tweet-date\">July 29, 2016</a>\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\" class=\"tweet-body\">Ali Bulac. {"content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><span class=\"drop-cap\"><span class=\"drop-cap__inner\">I</span></span> have convened a meeting of the <a href=\"https://www.britishirishcouncil.org/\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">British-Irish Council (BIC)</a> in Cardiff today to discuss the fundamental changes that will be brought about by the UK\u2019s exit from the European Union. The meeting has been labelled \u201cextraordinary\u201d by the council because it is ad hoc and relatively unplanned. However, today\u2019s meeting is truly set to be extraordinary because of its significance at this historic time for British politics.</p>\n<p>The British-Irish Council, which was created during the Northern Ireland peace process, has played a unique role in developing relationships and facilitating frank and open discussions between members. At this tumultuous time, it is more important than ever to maintain the strength of these relationships and work together to map out a successful way forward across our islands.</p>\n<p>Today\u2019s meeting will bring together leaders from both sides of the <a href=\"http://www.theguardian.com/politics/eu-referendum\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">EU referendum debate</a>, and includes representatives who already sit outside the EU. I am expecting debate to be full, frank and honest \u2013 an open arena where ideas and new approaches can be heard, as well as concerns aired.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">My message to business leaders is clear: keep your nerve, and keep investing in Wales</p>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>My absolute priority is protecting the Welsh economy and developing our trade links. Wales does business around the world and we aim to do more in the future, not less. Although there are challenges ahead, we are facing them from a position of strength. <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/mar/16/uk-unemployment-10-year-low-wage-growth-edges-up\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Unemployment is at a 10-year low</a> and our employment rate is outperforming all other parts of the UK, while Wales\u2019 economy boasts a strong international reputation as a place to invest. Already this year, announcements from <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/feb/24/james-bond-carmarker-aston-martin-to-open-wales-factory-for-dbx-model\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Aston Martin</a>, MotoNovo, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/mar/22/tvr-150-jobs-car-factory-wales-aston-martin\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">TVR</a>, Essentra, EE and BT have demonstrated our growing reputation as a great country to trade from.</p>\n<p>There is good news elsewhere, too. <a href=\"http://www.walesonline.co.uk/business/business-news/wales-turns-best-inward-investment-9345324\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Wales\u2019 inward investment performance</a> is better than ever, and our national airport in Cardiff has become the fastest-growing airport in the UK, which coincides with recent <a href=\"http://gov.wales/newsroom/businessandeconomy/2016/economy-secretary-celebrates-excellent-job-and-tourism-figures/?lang=en\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">record-breaking tourism figures</a>.</p>\n<p>For this momentum to continue, it is vital we retain uninterrupted access to the 500 million customers in the European single market. The importance of the single market cannot be understated \u2013 as I stressed to Theresa May when we met at the start of the week. During our meeting, I sought assurances from the prime minister over the <a href=\"http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-eu-referendum-36288638\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">half a billion pounds a year</a> that Wales currently receives from the EU. It is vital that the UK government guarantees every penny of this funding is safe.</p>\n<p>At today\u2019s meeting, I will share with members the immediate measures we have taken following the referendum and our ongoing strategy to protect jobs and maintain stability. This involves the introduction of six immediate measures to help provide assurance to our business community, including: expansion plans to support Welsh exports; looking anew at campaigns in Wales\u2019 overseas markets to promote inward investment; and developing new ways to boost national competitiveness.</p>\n<p>As part of our post-referendum economic strategy, on Monday I am holding a meeting of business leaders and trade unions to discuss how we can help them navigate the choppy waters ahead. My message to them is clear \u2013 keep your nerve, keep investing, and keep talking to us.</p>\n<p>Wales has a great deal to offer the world. As our <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/football/2016/jul/07/wales-team-set-for-heroes-welcome-in-cardiff-after-euro-2016-exit\" title=\"\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">recent footballing performance</a> in the Euro 2016 championship showed, we are no strangers to punching above our weight on the international stage. {"title": "Vincent van Gogh exhibition headlines National Gallery of Victoria 2017 program", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/artanddesign/2016/sep/16/vincent-van-gough-exhibition-headlines-national-gallery-of-victoria-2017-program", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>More than 60 artworks by Vincent van Gogh will be coming to the National Gallery of Victoria (NGV) in 2017, many of which have never been shown in Australia. </p>\n<p>The world premiere exhibition, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/artanddesign/van-gogh\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Van Gogh</a> and the Seasons, will be next year\u2019s instalment of the NGV\u2019s Winter Masterpieces series, comprised of 40 paintings and 25 drawings.</p>\n<p>Announced on Friday, the exhibition will be presented in four sections, devoted to each season, under the curation of art historian Sjraar van Heugten, former head of collections at the Van Gogh Museum. Works from van Gogh\u2019s own art collection will be included, along with additional documentary material.</p>\n<p>Tony Ellwood, director of the NGV, described it as a \u201ctrue coup\u201d for the gallery. </p>\n<p>\u201cVan Gogh was a true original. His love of the seasons was deeply profound and played an important role in his life and practice. This reverence for summer, autumn, winter and spring and the eternal cycles of nature is seen in the energy and dynamism of his distinct brushstrokes, which almost leap off the canvas with vitality.\u201d</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape element--supporting  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"d47a49ca454dcff593ee10a158f40526b2cede35\" id=\"img-2\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/d47a49ca454dcff593ee10a158f40526b2cede35/0_0_3000_2071/3000.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=69de1eae01dfaf27f540a5338fa3a01e\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"3000\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"2071\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-2\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nThe Great Wave by Japanese ukiyo-e artist Katsushika Hokusai. Photograph: NGV International\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>The announcement was made as the gallery\u2019s 2017 autumn/winter program was announced, including the most comprehensive exhibition of work by Katsushika Hokusai, the founding father of manga, seen in Australia. </p>\n<p>Opening in July 2017 and featuring 129 prints, four paintings and 10 rare books on loan from Japan\u2019s Ukiyo-e Museum in Matsumoto, the self-titled exhibition will be accompanied by a selection of Hokusai works from the NGV Collection, including his most famous image, A Great Wave.</p>\n<p>The NGV also announced Festival of Photography, which will take place in March across 11 gallery spaces and feature work by Bill Henson, Zo\u00eb Croggon and Patrick Pound, as well as William Eggleston Portraits, an Australian exclusive exhibition of the American photographer\u2019s work, which is <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/artanddesign/2016/jul/24/william-eggleston-portraits-review-national-portrait-gallery\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">currently showing</a> at the National Portrait Gallery in London.</p>\n<p>In December, NGV Australia will exhibit the work of a broad range of Indigenous artists in a group show, Who\u2019s Afraid Of Colour? With an in-depth focus on major female artists, including Julie Gough, Destiny Deacon, Emily Kam Kngwarray, Queenie McKenzie and Nonggirrnga Marawili, it will feature \u201cbold statements that explore colour and assert the politics of identity\u201d.</p>\n<p><em><span class=\"bullet\">\u2022</span> Van Gogh and the Seasons opens at NGV International on 28 April</em></p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "timestamp": "1474007236000", "author": "Steph Harmon", "summary": "More than 60 van Gogh artworks, many never shown in Australia before, are the centrepiece of an NGV autumn/winter program that also features Katsushika Hokusai and Festival of Photography"}

Australia 33-20 Argentina (Sanchez 72)</h2>\n<div class=\"block-elements block-elements--no-byline\" itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n<p>Another nice kick from Sanchez from wide out narrows the margin \u2014 but surely it\u2019s too late for the Pumas. </p>\n</div>\n\n<p class=\"block-share--liveblog-mobile\" data-open-overlay-on-click=\"share-modal-block-57dd2f13e4b0c762d480d5eb\" data-link-name=\"open mobile block share\">\n<button class=\"block-share__item--mobile button button--small button--tertiary mobile-only\">\nShare\n</button>\n</p>\n\n</div>\n<div id=\"block-57dd2e31e4b0df02df203289\" class=\"block block--content\" itemprop=\"liveBlogUpdate\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/BlogPosting\">\n<p class=\"block-time published-time\">\n<a href=\"/sport/live/2016/sep/17/rugby-championship-australia-v-argentina-live?page=with:block-57dd2e31e4b0df02df203289#block-57dd2e31e4b0df02df203289\" itemprop=\"url\" class=\"block-time__link\">\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T11:54:19.000Z\" data-relativeformat=\"med\" class=\" js-timestamp\" itemprop=\"datePublished\">9.54pm <span class=\"timezone\">AEST</span></time>\n<span class=\"block-time__absolute\">21:54</span>\n</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"block-elements block-elements--no-byline\" itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n<p><strong>71 min:</strong> A scrum penalty, against the Wallabies. The penalty count must be looking like a lunchtime cricket score about now.</p>\n<p>Hang on, the Pumas might have scored here. At the point of a rolling maul Isa is pushed try-wards and though he comes to ground short he manages to reach out and plant the ball on the line. This will be awarded...</p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"block-time updated-time\">Updated\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T12:28:52.000Z\">at 10.28pm AEST</time>\n</p>\n\n<p class=\"block-share--liveblog-mobile\" data-open-overlay-on-click=\"share-modal-block-57dd2e31e4b0df02df203289\" data-link-name=\"open mobile block share\">\n<button class=\"block-share__item--mobile button button--small button--tertiary mobile-only\">\nShare\n</button>\n</p>\n\n</div>\n<div id=\"block-57dd2dc3e4b0a8cdc62389d6\" class=\"block block--content\" itemprop=\"liveBlogUpdate\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/BlogPosting\">\n<p class=\"block-time published-time\">\n<a href=\"/sport/live/2016/sep/17/rugby-championship-australia-v-argentina-live?page=with:block-57dd2dc3e4b0a8cdc62389d6#block-57dd2dc3e4b0a8cdc62389d6\" itemprop=\"url\" class=\"block-time__link\">\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T11:51:05.000Z\" data-relativeformat=\"med\" class=\" js-timestamp\" itemprop=\"datePublished\">9.51pm <span class=\"timezone\">AEST</span></time>\n<span class=\"block-time__absolute\">21:51</span>\n</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"block-elements block-elements--no-byline\" itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n<p><strong>70 min: </strong>Two more penalties later, Argentina have a lineout throw 5m out from the Wallabies\u2019 line. With Tuculet approaching he chips over the top but he crashes to the ground when he hits the fullback who stood his ground. Folau chases but Argentina scramble and regain possession.</p>\n<p>Moore off, Polota-Nau on.</p>\n</div>\n\n<p class=\"block-share--liveblog-mobile\" data-open-overlay-on-click=\"share-modal-block-57dd27d4e4b0a8cdc62389b2\" data-link-name=\"open mobile block share\">\n<button class=\"block-share__item--mobile button button--small button--tertiary mobile-only\">\nShare\n</button>\n</p>\n\n</div>\n<div id=\"block-57dd2776e4b0c762d480d5cd\" class=\"block block--content\" itemprop=\"liveBlogUpdate\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/BlogPosting\">\n<p class=\"block-time published-time\">\n<a href=\"/sport/live/2016/sep/17/rugby-championship-australia-v-argentina-live?page=with:block-57dd2776e4b0c762d480d5cd#block-57dd2776e4b0c762d480d5cd\" itemprop=\"url\" class=\"block-time__link\">\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T11:23:37.000Z\" data-relativeformat=\"med\" class=\" js-timestamp\" itemprop=\"datePublished\">9.23pm <span class=\"timezone\">AEST</span></time>\n<span class=\"block-time__absolute\">21:23</span>\n</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"block-elements block-elements--no-byline\" itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n<p><strong>46 min:</strong> Creevy, as wide as he is tall, comes off, replaced by Montoya. {"title": "I faced the teacher who abused me when I was nine", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2016/sep/17/i-faced-the-teacher-who-abused-me-when-i-was-nine", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><span class=\"drop-cap\"><span class=\"drop-cap__inner\">J</span></span>ames is 6ft 5in tall, an imposing 45-year-old man with a successful career. He is a father of two young children and a popular, talented sportsman who excels at rugby and golf. If you got to know him well, you might discover a few quirks. He doesn\u2019t permit any black in his house. There won\u2019t ever be a leather sofa in his living room. He will never stock up on Jaffa Cakes for his kitchen cupboard. And he won\u2019t allow his four-year-old son to have a bunk bed.</p>\n<p>His partner, Emily, discovered the reason when she found him curled in a ball by their spare bed, a sweating \u201cgibbering wreck\u201d after they argued one day six years ago: \u201cI can still see him there, cowering, a big man, trying to get under the bed. He was like a little boy, whimpering, not lucid, as if he was in a flashback. I managed to get him on to the bed and held him, which normally he doesn\u2019t let me do. That was a pivotal moment, seeing what was going on in his head.\u201d</p>\n<p>In the first year of their relationship, James hinted that he\u2019d had a horrible time at school. Emily wasn\u2019t given the whole story at once but, gradually, the secret that he\u2019d kept close for more than 30 years came out: the physical and sexual abuse he\u2019d suffered when he was nine years old.</p>\n<p>In 1980, James\u2019s parents, a businessman and a teacher, decided that their eldest son would benefit from a private education at a boarding school in Suffolk. St George\u2019s was an impressive-looking former stately home with a sweeping drive. On his first night, he and other homesick boys were hauled out of their metal bunk-beds by two prefects. Wearing slippers, a dressing gown and starchy new pyjamas, James was led along corridors until he came to a black door beneath a winding staircase. They could hear\u00a0crying.</p>\n<p>Inside was a long leather sofa, a big desk on which lay a cane and a contraption that resembled an oversized table-tennis bat and two men: Derek Slade, the headmaster, and Gerard Singer, the head of languages. James does not like to call them by their names. For him, it dignifies them. \u201cI built up such a resilience to them. I\u2019d prefer \u2018him\u2019 to be \u2018it\u2019,\u201d he says.</p>\n<p>James was ordered to turn around and drop his trousers. Then he was whacked with \u201csix of the best\u201d. After a few weeks and more beatings \u2013 \u201cyou\u2019re punished for crying, you\u2019re punished for not having your shoes polished, it was all very regimented\u201d \u2013 James was summoned again to the room with the black door. There, waiting, were the same two teachers.</p>\n<p>\u201cI knocked on the black door and walked into the room and Slade was behind his desk. My normal thing was to go and adopt my position and drop my trousers, and I stood there waiting. I didn\u2019t take much notice but his trousers were round his ankles. I was waiting for the cane and he came over and thrust his penis into me and that was the first time he raped me.\u201d</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">My relationships haven\u2019t been intimate or cuddly. I look at other couples and it tortures me that I\u2019m unable to do that</p>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>James uses such unequivocal language now because, in the witness box of Ipswich crown court, where Singer finally stood trial earlier this summer, James was told by the judge that he had to speak more plainly. \u201cSeveral times, the judge said, \u2018You have to say what he is doing.\u2019 In court, you have to be graphic and say \u2018penis\u2019 and \u2018penis inside you\u2019 and \u2018semen\u2019.\u201d</p>\n<p>That was a shock to James: he hadn\u2019t been warned in advance by the Crown Prosecution Service, for whom he was a key witness.</p>\n<p>After the abuse, James was sent back to his dorm. \u201cAs you walk out of the door, there was a table with Jaffa Cakes. They said, \u2018Take three Jaffa Cakes\u2019. When you\u2019re away from home and the school meals are absolutely awful, a Jaffa Cake was like Willy Wonka\u2019s Golden Ticket.\u201d</p>\n<p>James was raped between 25 and 30 times by both teachers in a year, before they abruptly left the school without explanation. \u201cYou go home at Christmas just a broken child. I just can\u2019t get excited by Christmas now. All these things have triggers in later life.\u201d</p>\n<p>After they fell in love, Emily became used to James\u2019s reluctance to be tactile. Their first house had a galley kitchen. \u201cYou just can\u2019t share that space. It\u2019s like a forcefield around him. He will flinch if I go to touch him,\u201d she says. \u201cJames is not in any way violent or physically abusive. I\u2019ve never feared that he would be to any of us, but there is a swirling vortex of negative energy around him. It comes into the room with him and it\u2019s bigger than him.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cMy relationships haven\u2019t been intimate or cuddly, I don\u2019t do all that,\u201d says James. \u201cHolding hands, touching someone\u2019s shoulder at a party, which is normal in normal relationships, is not normal for me. I look at other couples and it tortures me that I\u2019m not able to do that.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cIt also tortures me to see the closeness between other couples,\u201d adds Emily. \u201cI desperately want it too. Living like this is very lonely.\u201d</p>\n<p>Around the time Emily came to understand his past, James discovered several old schoolmates on Facebook discussing the arrest of their former headmaster, Derek Slade. \u201cI was really struggling with life. I was near Ipswich, where the trial was, and went into the public gallery. I saw this shrivelled old man with a big Santa Claus beard in the dock. I looked at him and he looked at me. It put the fear of God into me. I just got up and walked out.\u201d</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"63ec5a619e78d806d37ab69bad907edc0e5cc694\" id=\"img-2\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/63ec5a619e78d806d37ab69bad907edc0e5cc694/0_0_5574_3344/5574.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=63b0492874d4031a93257ae8bf9f3c3b\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"5574\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3344\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-2\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nGiving evidence in court was harrowing for James but afterwards, \u2018the weight went from my shoulders,\u2019 he says. Photograph: Posed by model/Getty Images\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>Slade\u2019s conviction \u2013 jailed for 21 years \u2013 \u201ctriggered something\u201d in James, and he resolved to do something about his second abuser, Gerard Singer.</p>\n<p>He went to the police and spent hours giving evidence and undergoing medical examinations (doctors\u2019 evidence formed part of the prosecution against Singer). Although Emily knew about his childhood trauma, James was still reluctant to share the progress of his case, which took six years to come to trial. He was upset when a new police liaison officer casually asked him what his case was about (she hadn\u2019t bothered to check) and when he was told there wasn\u2019t time to visit the court before the trial to familiarise himself with the surroundings. \u201cI felt I was always chasing the police,\u201d he says. \u201cI was expecting a bit more support. Since the trial, I\u2019ve heard nothing from them.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cQuite often things would be terrible between us and only afterwards it would transpire that something had happened with the police or the court case,\u201d says Emily. \u201cI\u2019ve tried many times to ask him about his experiences. On the one hand, I have to be sensitive and not pry. On the other, I\u2019ve been pushed away quite venomously so many times, I\u2019m reluctant to put myself there. He keeps himself this closed book. I\u2019m a very open person but in order to preserve my own sanity I\u2019ve had to emotionally turn away.\u201d</p>\n<p>In this way, the abuse \u201cdoesn\u2019t stop when it stopped 35 years ago\u201d, says Emily. \u201cThe evil is still within our family because it has its impact on him and his behaviour and we\u2019re living with that every day.\u201d</p>\n<p>James, she says, is \u201cquite reluctant\u201d to seek help. At first, they tried couples counselling but Emily says it didn\u2019t really work. She believes he needs specialist counselling. \u201cIt takes him a long time to build up trust in the counsellor,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p>Giving evidence against his abuser in court was \u201cthe most harrowing thing I\u2019ve had to do in my life,\u201d says James. \u201cIt could go two ways. You could be believed or you could be back in there for contempt of court.\u201d</p>\n<p>On the day he was called to give evidence, their four-year-old son, Billy, could tell he was upset.</p>\n<p>James and Emily told him that Daddy had to sort out some problems at work. Billy disappeared and then returned. \u201cI\u2019ve got something for you Daddy. I\u2019ve got Captain Barnacles. He\u2019s there to protect you.\u201d</p>\n<p>James put Captain Barnacles \u2013 the leader of the Octonauts cartoon \u2013 in his pocket when he stood in the witness box. \u201cWhen it was getting harrowing, I pulled him out and just broke down. I said to the jury, \u2018I\u2019ve got a four-year-old boy and a 10-month-old girl who are in this big world and I\u2019m going to do my damnedest to protect them.\u2019\u201d</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">I\u2019ve suffered torment. Most importantly, James \u2013 and eight other abused former pupils who gave evidence \u2013 was believed. Singer was found guilty of all 27 counts of abuse. He was sentenced to 21 years in prison and a further eight on licence.</p>\n<p>\u201cI\u2019ve suffered torment of a great magnitude. The physical side of things is never going to heal,\u201d says James. \u201cWhen a child comes to you, stop and listen. We can never eradicate evil but we can always listen.\u201d</p>\n<p>After the trial, they went on holiday and Emily caught a \u201cglimpse\u201d of a happier future for their family. \u201cJames was open and communicative and perceptive and he understood how we could have a normal conversation about things and the life going on around him. I\u2019d been living with this block of stone for four years and now he was starting to show some emotion. You don\u2019t want to see someone hurting but it\u2019s preferable to them blocking it out and taking it out on everyone around them.\u201d</p>\n<p>However, \u201cThat kind of closed again,\u201d says Emily. \u201cI never expected everything to be instantly better. We had this amazing breakthrough. It was impossible for that to last because it can\u2019t be that easy [to get over abuse].\u201d</p>\n<p>Emily worries about the impact of a \u201ctoxic atmosphere\u201d on their children. \u201cI want the home to be a place of sanctuary for the children, not stress. This is the point at which things have to start moving forward or else he is never going to change. He needs to see what he has to lose. Do you want that terrible thing that happened in the past to ruin your future? Don\u2019t let those people ruin any more of your life.\u201d</p>\n<p>What of his parents, who sent him to the school in the first place?</p>\n<p>Ten years ago, when James\u2019s parents bailed him out of a serious debt, his mother asked him what was wrong and he finally told her about the abuse. He says he and his father don\u2019t have a very close bond but doesn\u2019t blame his parents for sending him away and shows me an email from his father, expressing his love, support and admiration for his son. \u201cThey did what they thought was best. She\u2019s never seen that part of me and I\u2019ve never seen that part of me. I want to put all of this dark stuff in a box. The sex is amazing, which is why we\u2019ve continued for so long. We are intellectually matched and get on very well, but neither of us want the relationship to be anything more than it is. I feel lucky to have what I have with him. I am independent and very happy not to be in a \u201cnormal\u201d relationship. I work overseas a lot and having him to satisfy me when I am back is perfect. I am very content with all aspects of my life.</p>\n<p>However, I know that the relationship will come to a natural conclusion at some point. As that time gets closer (we don\u2019t have a fixed date, but we are not getting any younger), I wonder how I will feel. Yes, I will be immensely sad to have lost a special, intimate relationship but I am not sure if I will suddenly want to share my life with someone full-time. If I do, how will I go about finding that next someone? I will have such high expectations that I wonder if I will ever find another man who can make me feel satisfied \u2013 both sexually and emotionally. I don\u2019t want what I have to stop, but I know that is not possible. {"title": "Julie Bishop says Australia will look elsewhere if US doesn't pass trade deal", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/17/julie-bishop-says-australia-will-look-elsewhere-if-us-doesnt-pass-trade-deal", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>Australia will seek out alternative free trade agreements in the region should the Trans-Pacific Partnership fail to pass a US Congress vote, the foreign affairs minister, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/julie-bishop\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Julie Bishop</a>, has said.</p>\n<p>Bishop made the comments while addressing reporters in Washington, where she has met representatives for US presidential candidates Hillary Clinton and Donald Trump. She will also meet the US Secretary of State, John Kerry, and attend US president Barack Obama\u2019s leaders\u2019 summit on refugees in New York.</p>\n<p>Clinton and Trump oppose the 12-country Trans-Pacific Partnership, saying the deal is not in the US interest. However Obama is committed to passing the agreement through the Congress and Senate before his term ends.</p>\n<p>Bishop said she had urged the Trump and Clinton camps to view the deal as \u201cnot only economically important but strategically vital for our region\u201d.</p>\n<p>\u201cI had a fairly sympathetic hearing from all of the representatives who see that free trade is the basis of US economic success,\u201d she said.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-2 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Trans-Pacific Partnership provisions 'questionable', says Productivity Commission</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/jul/25/trans-pacific-partnership-provisions-questionable-says-productivity-commission\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>\u201cCountries like Australia need to continue to press the case for liberalised trade and I believe the Trans-Pacific Partnership is a comprehensive high quality agreement that will be of benefit to the people of United States in appropriating more jobs and economic growth.\u201d</p>\n<p>If Obama failed to pass the agreement and her appeals to the presidential candidates proved unsuccessful, Bishop said Australia would be looking for other free trade agreements \u201cand continuing our quest for a free trade zone in this part of the world, in the Asia-Pacific\u201d. </p>\n<p>\u201cThere is the regional comprehensive economic partnership that is being promoted by the ASEAN countries of south-east Asia, but we still want to see the Trans-Pacific Partnership pass through the US Congress and we\u2019re certainly urging both the Clinton and the Trump camps to do just that,\u201d she said.</p>\n<p>\u201cBut in the meantime, president Obama has made it clear that he will seek to pass it through the period from the presidential election through to the inauguration.\u201d</p>\n<p>The opposition leader, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/bill-shorten\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Bill Shorten</a>, is also in Washington meeting US officials. Asked by reporters whether Labor would support the deal, Shorten said the opposition would wait to see if the US ratified the accord and also for the findings of Australia\u2019s Senate inquiry into the Trans-Pacific Partnership before endorsing it.</p>\n<p>Bishop was also pressed by reporters about who Australia would be supporting for the UN Secretary-General position, after the prime minister, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/jul/29/malcolm-turnbull-kevin-rudd-un-secretary-general-nomination\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Malcolm Turnbull, declined in July</a> to endorse the former Labor prime minister Kevin Rudd for the role. Bishop had supported Rudd\u2019s nomination, though she did not endorse his campaign.</p>\n<p>\u201cWe haven\u2019t made a decision because there are still a number of opportunities for other candidates to put their names forward and I imagine that over the coming weeks we\u2019ll see more candidates, not less,\u201d she said.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link Trump had long fanned the flames of this conspiracy theory, known as \u2018birtherism\u2019, and spent much of spring 2011 <a href=\"http://www.nytimes.com/2016/07/03/us/politics/donald-trump-birther-obama.html?_r=0\" data-link-name=\"in standfirst link\" class=\"u-underline\">garnering media attention</a> by constantly claiming without any evidence that Obama might have born overseas. He then sporadically revisited the issue in the years to come. We look back at some of Trump\u2019s more incendiary remarks </p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "timestamp": "1474061536000", "author": "Chris Whitworth", "summary": "A look back at Donald Trump\u2019s various conspiracies about Barack Obama\u2019s place of birth"}
{"title": "Meeting Pauline Hanson's voters: silent screamers find their voice", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/17/meeting-pauline-hansons-voters-silent-screamers-find-their-voice", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><span class=\"drop-cap\"><span class=\"drop-cap__inner\">K</span></span>errie Young\u2019s great yearning in life was to be a rock star. Instead, at 59 years of age, she finds herself as a housewife in Brisbane with two adult children she adores but is confounded by. Her daughter, a Christian convert who is on a scholarship at university, does not \u201cdrink, smoke or have sex\u201d, a puzzled Kerrie says. Her husband thinks Kerrie\u2019s a redneck.</p>\n<p>Young has been a lifelong Labor voter, but at the last election she cast her No 1 Senate vote for Pauline Hanson\u2019s One Nation party. The future terrifies her.</p>\n<p>She is dreadfully nervous about being interviewed as one of the people who voted for Hanson. She speaks quickly at the beginning, looking away and laughing defensively when making certain statements. But she thinks the issue is too important not to speak out about, to try to warn people, to hopefully be at the start of what will become a national conversation.<br/></p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Pauline Hanson is back, and it's still just as hard to counter her rhetoric with facts</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/10/pauline-hanson-is-back-and-its-still-just-as-hard-to-counter-her-rhetoric-with-facts\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>\u201cI don\u2019t think there\u2019s enough awareness of my generation having been told all our lives, paying taxes, paying into superannuation, you can retire, you can get in your bus and travel around, you can go on cruises or whatever, now all of a sudden \u2013 boom \u2013 you can\u2019t. I want to know why,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cMy friend said retirement is not a right, retirement is a privilege and I can\u2019t see that. If we have all paid our taxes, if our parents have paid their taxes, why are we sending the money overseas, why are we bringing in refugees who I read somewhere it cost $60,000 to each set up.</p>\n<p> \u201cThis is my money. This is our money.\u201d</p>\n<p> With her hair in a neat braid, wearing glasses and a simple floral shirt, Young holds forth on all of her fears while sipping a chai latte in a suburban Brisbane shopping centre. Her retirement. Foreign investment. Immigration. Mining destroying arable farming lands. She is one of roughly 134,000 who gave Hanson a first preference vote in Queensland. The hundreds of thousands who cast votes for her One Nation party Australia-wide <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/jul/03/australias-double-dissolution-election-backfires-badly-with-likely-senate-makeup\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">delivered four One Nation representatives into the Senate </a>with the chance to have a powerful influence in a chamber where the government has not got a majority. <strong> <br/></strong></p>\n<p>In the spirit of most dogmatic people <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/10/pauline-hanson-is-back-and-its-still-just-as-hard-to-counter-her-rhetoric-with-facts\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Hanson has not let facts get in the way of her cause</a>. She has <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/video/2016/sep/14/pauline-hanson-australia-in-danger-of-being-swamped-by-muslims-video\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">warned of Australia being swamped by Muslims</a> when they make up 2.2% of the population. In the 1990s Hanson\u2019s focus was on Asians \u2013 so far she has not explained what happened to the supposed invasion of the 1990s. She has linked organised crime, welfare fraud, unemployment and the prison population to Muslims without producing data or evidence to back her claims.</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"83a92c07bd5865ad91dc28681cee0bf64c4a9c1f\" id=\"img-2\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/83a92c07bd5865ad91dc28681cee0bf64c4a9c1f/0_0_4500_3000/4500.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=a9731bb624c74671fa555e24356a239f\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"4500\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3000\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-2\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nPauline Hanson delivers her maiden speech in the Senate on Wednesday. Photograph: Mike Bowers for the Guardian\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>Rising inequality, coupled with the ability to create communities of people who live tens of thousands kilometres apart through social media, has made a fertile patch for Hanson to flourish in.</p>\n<h2>Divided by geography, united by fear</h2>\n<p>Young is a housewife whose husband has dealt with health issues for many years, meaning periods where he has not been able to work.</p>\n<p>Robyn McLaughlin is an amputee recovering from cancer.</p>\n<p>Graham (not his real name) lost his livelihood when he was punched on a night out and acquired a brain injury that meant he was not allowed to work in his manual labour industry anymore.</p>\n<p>Shirley\u2019s daughter looked for work on years after finishing university while Shirley looked on helplessly until one day her daughter suggested they both kill themselves.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">It\u2019s very, very difficult these days to express anything without sounding racist or non-PC</p>\n<footer>\n<cite class=\"pullquote-cite\">Kerrie Young</cite>\n</footer>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104
