9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>They live scattered across the country, from Western Australia to Newcastle to Townsville, but they all say almost the exact same thing when asked why they voted for Hanson. The economy. They are worried about their futures and terrified for their children\u2019s. Where are they going to live? What jobs are they going to have? How are they going to survive?</p>\n<p>Fuelled by posts on social media, particularly Facebook, they have discovered what they think the root of their problems is \u2013 foreign investment and asset sales. This segues into concern about immigration.</p>\n<p>While Malcolm Turnbull has been talking innovation and Bill Shorten has been pitching to the middle class, those becoming poorer and feeling the class lines shifting under their feet, have had just one person listening to them. They don\u2019t just read Hanson\u2019s Facebook page, they are talking to her. She is talking to them. Hanson responds to multiple comments every day, reassuring people who are upset about particular policies and situations, arguing with people who disagree with her and seemingly taking them into her confidence (\u201cI don\u2019t handle compliments very well\u201d) while her fans tell her they are concerned about immigration, politician wages (\u201ccut them across the board to the average Australian\u2019s wages\u201d) or offering Hanson advice (\u201cI notice you get quite flustered when you are upset or angry, try mindfulness breathing\u201d). </p>\n<p>Or they just talk to her as they would any of their other mates on Facebook. \u201cGood job getting the tea in without looking, really good technique.\u201d</p>\n<p> Young has befriended people as part of the community and has had Hanson respond personally to her messages and comments. Young\u2019s political beliefs are a patchwork that don\u2019t follow the conventional patterns \u2013 she does not really care about marriage equality either way, is passionate about the environment, suspicious of immigration and upset by foreign investment. </p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape element--showcase  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"b232714f6a3896857e79cdb6ef87789b27d044e8\" id=\"img-3\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/b232714f6a3896857e79cdb6ef87789b27d044e8/0_0_4096_2747/4096.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=bf0df9fa07df0b2708bcec7a043b45c1\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"4096\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"2747\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-3\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nPauline Hanson jokingly hides behind one of her campaign signs, surrounded by supporters, during her election-night function in Ipswich, west of Brisbane. Photograph: Dan Peled/EPA\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>She seems slightly surprised at how her life has turned out and will often start ruminating on that while answering questions about policy. At one stage while talking about Indigenous Australians she diverts and reveals she has seen my Facebook profile. \u201cI looked at your wedding photos, you looked so beautiful and happy, I hope you never lose that fresh loveliness, but you will. Nobody gets out of here without a bit of pain.\u201d </p>\n<p>Hanson\u2019s One Nation has been Young\u2019s personal middle ground between parties that have let her down. She will not vote Greens as she does not think they talk about the environment enough and she will not vote Nationals because she thinks they don\u2019t believe in climate change. She has never voted Liberal and she is appalled by Labor\u2019s behaviour over the past six years and does not think there is any talent there anyway.</p>\n<p>\u201cThe rot set in when they all ganged up on Kevin Rudd, everybody I know says Kevin Rudd is a real prick, blah blah blah, if you can\u2019t work with him maybe it\u2019s your problem? Truly brilliant people are really hard to for normal people to deal with, look at Paul Keating. Everyone thought he was an asshole too, but he is brilliant.\u201d</p>\n<p> Young thinks Australia does not have the resources to support many more people and there should be a temporary stop to immigration, as well as an examination of the welfare system. When it comes to these issues, her angst could almost be <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/14/pauline-hanson-first-speech-senate-calls-for-immigration-ban\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">lifted directly from Hanson\u2019s maiden speech</a>.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">All the businesses are gone, car manufacturing is gone, sugar is gone, everything\u2019s gone for that little bit of money</p>\n<footer>\n<cite class=\"pullquote-cite\">Shirley</cite>\n</footer>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p> \u201cThe ones who are working are getting taxed more and more to pay for the people who aren\u2019t working, it\u2019s just untenable, it\u2019s not possible to keep going that way. It\u2019s like if you get a fish tank and they\u2019ve got too many fish in it, they start eating each other. That\u2019s what happens,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cIt\u2019s very, very difficult these days to express anything without sounding racist or non-PC. I wouldn\u2019t hurt anybody, I don\u2019t care what you do in your own time, I honestly believe there is a section out there who stop any intelligent debate by throwing these \u2018vile racist bigot\u2019 comments around. Is there a way to express disapproval of certain value systems and certain belief systems without sounding racist? Is there a way of doing it? Or do you just have to wear it? I\u2019ve been called that, my friend that I walk with every day calls me her redneck friend. And I say to her \u2018are you aware that this happens in Islam? Do you understand what Eid is?\u2019\u201d</p>\n<h2>\u2018We\u2019re selling Australia\u2019</h2>\n<p>Young is also called a redneck by her husband and the mocking by people close to her is common to other Hanson voters. Further north on the Sunshine Coast Shirley talks in a granny flat she is housesitting.<br/></p>\n<p> Shirley\u2019s daughter does not know that she votes Hanson (\u201cI would never tell her, she supports Muslims\u201d) and Shirley is careful before she tells friends, sounding them out first to see if they already agree with her on other issues.</p>\n<p> As she welcomes me at the door she tells me she has been researching my name and knows it is Lebanese. \u201cIs your father a Muslim?\u201d she asks narrowing her eyes. To her small comfort the family were Maronite Christian when they arrived in Australia.</p>\n<p> \u201c[Hanson is] interested in what I\u2019m interested in which is the selling of Australia, I don\u2019t mind foreign investment but our land is going, if you go to another country you can\u2019t buy the land \u2026 Australia is just too open,\u201d she says.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 2\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Pauline Hanson emerges as the queen of a potentially unruly Senate | Katharine Murphy</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/aug/04/pauline-hanson-emerges-as-the-queen-of-a-potentially-unruly-senate\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>A short and talkative woman who cheerfully describes herself as fat, Shirley is 66 and retired. She has lived in Cairns and Sydney before settling on the Sunshine Coast and voted Labor until she switched to One Nation at the last election. She is also a Sri Lankan immigrant.</p>\n<p> \u201cI got out of Sydney because people thought I was Muslim, and I get Muslim men looking at me, I started to feel treated differently, in shops people weren\u2019t serving me,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cI got this in Cairns in the 70s \u2026 I remember getting an ice cream for my little girl, who\u2019s really white, can\u2019t go in the sun \u2026 they could see me, it was packed this ice cream shop, all these people were behind me, these girls were serving everyone in the shop except for me. </p>\n<p>\u201cI got really sick of it, I said really loud \u2018Am I too short? Am I too black for you to serve me?\u2019 It happened so many times in Cairns, it really did. We were classed as Aboriginal, we were treated as Aboriginal, which was not very nice. </p>\n<p> \u201cThere\u2019s still racism here, I feel it I know it and I don\u2019t care.\u201d</p>\n<p> So does she have any empathy for how Muslim people, and Aboriginal people, may feel about Hanson and her comments? She concedes Hanson \u201ccame across as racist\u201d in the 1990s in the way she spoke about Aboriginal people but what Hanson really wanted was equality for all, not for one group (Indigenous people) to be treated differently from other Australians by getting certain welfare payments.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">It\u2019s about time Australians stood ground for their own country</p>\n<footer>\n<cite class=\"pullquote-cite\">Graham</cite>\n</footer>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>\u201cShe said you\u2019re gonna lose Australia, Australia is going to be lost, and all these yeas later she\u2019s absolutely right, we\u2019re selling Australia. It\u2019s OK to have foreign investments, but all the businesses are gone, car manufacturing is gone, sugar is gone, everything\u2019s gone for that little bit of money, they\u2019ve sold it,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cThey\u2019re sending everything offshore where it\u2019s cheaper, so it\u2019s not Australians getting employed, the mining, they\u2019re employing people on 457 visas, I think it\u2019s the worst thing ever, that loophole.\u201d</p>\n<p> Shirley\u2019s primary concern is foreign investment but while others want to ban all immigration as an extension of that, or loathe Muslims, she is more tepid. She tells a story of being glared at by a woman in a headscarf to illustrate her point about some of them not being trustworthy.</p>\n<p>\u201cStop the people from coming at the moment, but they\u2019re not all bad, I know some good ones, and they agree, because they say \u2018we don\u2019t know who\u2019s coming in\u2019, they consider themselves Australian. They don\u2019t want sharia law, these are Muslims talking to me, the average Australian does not want it, they\u2019re too scared to say anything,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p>\u201cI\u2019m not a politician, I\u2019m not an accountant, I\u2019m not anybody who knows anything but I see stuff and think \u2018that doesn\u2019t look right to me\u2019, the average Joe Blow feels things more than they actually understand or know, they feel things, they know stuff.\u201d </p>\n<h2>Hardship, hard yards and grievance unheeded</h2>\n<p>Most of Hanson\u2019s supporters do just \u201cknow stuff\u201d. A lot of their news, like most people\u2019s, comes from Facebook. But theirs is dissected by rightwing blogs and sites. Their world view is reinforced on pages such as Hanson\u2019s and their own invitation-only private groups with more than 10,000 people congregating on one.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 3\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Comprehending Pauline is not the challenge. Engaging constructively with Hansonism is | Katharine Murphy</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2016/sep/14/comprehending-pauline-is-not-the-challenge-engaging-constructively-with-hansonism-is\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p> They are mostly older than 50, mostly live in regional areas, and have not had easy lives. Their grievances, real and imagined, make up the bedrock of their politics. For a long time they have not felt voiceless, but that they have been screaming and nobody is listening to them.</p>\n<p>They are driven by their own circumstance, the greater good and other people do not really factor into it. It\u2019s about what they have lost, what\u2019s slipped through their fingers, what their children are going to miss out on. They don\u2019t have the luxury of worrying about other people.</p>\n<p> In Newcastle, Robyn McLaughlin is recovering from chemotherapy after being diagnosed with cancer while getting treatment related to her amputated right leg. She has long been faithful to the minor parties and voted for Hanson in the 1990s, for much the same reasons that she votes for her now.</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"dc2909c189a38e78ac09506306d4e250c0b865ff\" id=\"img-4\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/dc2909c189a38e78ac09506306d4e250c0b865ff/0_0_5376_3024/5376.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=e6c70321a02af50eea91d0826c317cea\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"5376\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3024\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-4\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nHanson speaks at a rally against Islam in Brisbane in April 2015. Photograph: Jamie McKinnell/AAP\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p> \u201cBringing all these so-called refugees into the country there\u2019s no infrastructure to support what we\u2019ve got here, it\u2019s already been drained. I\u2019m a baby boomer, I\u2019ve worked all my life, I\u2019ve done the hard yards, I\u2019ve paid taxes and yet because I\u2019ve saved money and been taught to be sensible for a rainy day I can\u2019t even get a disability pension, it\u2019s quite unfair. Myself aside, there\u2019s pensioners, veterans, kids on street and all this is being ignored and we\u2019re bringing in all these people, they don\u2019t want to integrate,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> The 67-year-old is a dyed-in-the-wool Hanson supporter who she says she pays extra to go to a butcher that uses a halal free abattoir and that the Trans-Pacific Partnership agreement \u201cfits nicely into the global governance that the UN is pushing\u201d.</p>\n<p> Graham is another who, having taken body blow after body blow throughout his life, is easily convinced of the existence of villains and Hanson is happy to supply them. Graham suffered an acquired brain injury after being punched in 2001 and though he has recovered his speech and motor skills he is not allowed to work in the maritime industry. After, as he puts it, being followed by the black dog for a number of years, he is rebuilding his life in Western Australia. But he is worried. He is worried about how he is going to keep finding work, he is worried about his daughters on the other side of the country in Victoria, he is worried he could get hit again, he is worried about what could happen next, and he is worried about Muslims.</p>\n<p> \u201cPrimary schools are going visiting mosques, that\u2019s trying to encourage kids and speaking about their religion, and then when you see their side of Islam and what they do actually believe in is pretty disgusting. Such as against the females, they are not being able to wear a bikini, they see someone wearing a pair of shorts and they think they have the right to rape them,\u201d he says.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">It\u2019s just so much easier to call her a racist bigot rather than actually think about something and do something</p>\n<footer>\n<cite class=\"pullquote-cite\">Kerrie Young</cite>\n</footer>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p> \u201cIt\u2019s totally wrong. They turned their religion into a violent religion. It\u2019s about time Australians stood ground for their own country, my grandfather and great uncles didn\u2019t go to war to let other societies into our country to change our religion and the way we live our free life.</p>\n<p> \u201cI worry about my kids and their kids, putting all these mosques around Australia. All of a sudden they will be putting their votes in and they won\u2019t allow our Anzacs to sell or pledge their poppies or raise concerns.\u201d </p>\n<p> Graham is strident in his political beliefs but does not want his full name printed like many other Hanson supporters. They say they don\u2019t feel ashamed voting for Hanson but most have people very close to them who do not know how they vote.</p>\n<p> They see the election of Hanson as a final stand, one of their very last chances to be heard, a slight possibility that maybe the future will be OK. They feel Hanson understands them, and to many Hanson voters, what they feel is crucial.</p>\n<p>Back in the suburban shopping centre Young sighs and looks past the shoulder of the person sitting next to her when she talks about the reaction to her choice to vote for Hanson.</p>\n<p>\u201cPeople immediately, many people, the minute you mention <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/pauline-hanson\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Pauline Hanson</a> roll their eyes and call her a racist or a yobbo, or that stupid woman \u2026 she\u2019s xenophobic.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 4\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Pauline Hanson's maiden speech to the Australian Senate \u2013 full text</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/pauline-hansons-maiden-speech-to-the-australian-senate-full-text\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>\u201cNo, she\u2019s someone who feels something [but] who wasn\u2019t educated enough to know the big words, that\u2019s all. I really believe her heart is in the right place and what she\u2019s trying to say, is very, very pertinent to how we should be thinking bout the future but it\u2019s just so much easier to call her a racist bigot rather than actually think about something and do something about something that is going to affect you and your children.\u201d</p>\n<p>Hanson\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/politicians-and-muslim-leaders-condemn-hanson-she-doesnt-know-what-shes-talking-about\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">views are inflammatory</a>, divisive and simplistic. But while her supporters\u2019 views can be out of step with mainstream Australia, they constitute a growing minority that needs to be acknowledged. Labor and Liberal parties have had falling primary votes since the early 1990s and at the most recent election One Nation recorded a higher primary vote in Queensland than the Greens. Just <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/politicians-and-muslim-leaders-condemn-hanson-she-doesnt-know-what-shes-talking-about\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">condemning Hanson</a> is not enough; there is an argument to be properly explained and won. The people who vote for Hanson, mostly from increasingly marginalised communities, are ignored at the country\u2019s peril. </p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "timestamp": "1474064554000", "author": "Bridie Jabour", "summary": "Bridie Jabour travels in search of the people who brought One Nation back into parliament, scattered across the country and with a variety of experiences but with real and imagined grievances at the bedrock of their politics"}
{"title": "W-League to introduce player minimum wage standards: FFA boss", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/football/2016/sep/17/w-league-to-introduce-player-mimimum-wage-standards-ffa-boss", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>Football Federation Australia has signalled for the first time it wants to bring in a collective bargaining agreement (CBA) for <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/football/w-league\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">W-League</a> players.</p>\n<p>And the national women\u2019s football league could expand in size and length if there\u2019s the money to support it.</p>\n<p>W-League chiefs, players \u2013 through Professional Footballers Australia (PFA) \u2013 and W-League clubs have established a new taskforce to find a pathway to professionalism.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-1 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">'Vast' gender wage gap still exists within billion-dollar sports industry</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2016/sep/15/vast-gender-wage-gap-still-exists-within-billion-dollar-sports-industry\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>Unlike Socceroos, Matildas and A-League players, W-League players are without a formalised pay deal.</p>\n<p>FFA has admitted that many players have been playing for free in past competitions, with most clubs paying an average wage below $150 a week.</p>\n<p>PFA has long called for the institution of a league-wide CBA \u2013 which enshrines wage standards and conditions \u2013 and it appears to have won the fight.</p>\n<p>On the taskforce\u2019s agenda are four areas \u2013 league structure and format, club infrastructure and player conditions \u2013 with agreed targets to be set in each.</p>\n<p>FFA chief executive David Gallop affirmed the sport\u2019s commitment to female football while announcing the new \u201cworking party\u201d in a statement on Saturday morning.</p>\n<p>\u201cFootball has had a national women\u2019s league since we launched the Westfield W-League in 2008/9 and has enjoyed strong growth,\u201d he said.</p>\n<p>In fact, Gallop sold FFA\u2019s commitment short, given it ran the National Women\u2019s Soccer League from 1996-2004.</p>\n<p>\u201cThe common goal of the FFA and the PFA is to lead the way by also establishing a CBA for the national league players. One of the tasks of the Working Party will be to set a realistic timeframe and basis for achieving this,\u201d Gallop said.</p>\n<p>The move sets up football to \u2013 both commercially and for talented athletes \u2013 with netball and AFL, which are establishing new national women\u2019s leagues in 2017, and cricket.</p>\n<p>Newly appointed W-League chief Greg O\u2019Rourke suggested his primary concern was ensuring financial viability.</p>\n<p>\u201cThe focus now is on building a league which is sustainable but more professional on many levels to ensure growth for clubs and players alike,\u201d he said.</p>\n<p>\u201cWe need to ensure the platform allows us to move to more games for the players and fans with the addition of more rounds and potentially more teams.</p>\n<p>PFA boss John Didulica said he wanted to build \u201ca women\u2019s football competition of global significance\u201d that would improve the Matildas.</p>\n<p>\u201cBuilding the W-League into a sustainable professional competition will establish a platform for the hundreds of thousands of young girls currently playing football and ensure our ongoing international success,\u201d he said.</p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "timestamp": "1474087591000", "author": "Australian Associated Press", "summary": "Football Federation Australia has signalled for the first time it wants to bring in a collective bargaining agreement (CBA) for W-League players"}
{"timestamp": "1474007635000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2016/sep/16/when-we-walked-out-on-pauline-hanson-we-reached-out-to-decent-australians", "author": "Richard Di Natale", "title": "When we walked out on Pauline Hanson, we reached out to decent Australians", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><span class=\"drop-cap\"><span class=\"drop-cap__inner\">\u201cG</span></span>o home you greasy wog!\u201d. Those words, yelled at me in anger by classmates who didn\u2019t know any better, still sting. This didn\u2019t happen often, and not nearly as often as my parents\u2019 generation experienced, but for me it was a taste of what racism is and does. Racism is hateful and it damages people.</p>\n<p>What <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/pauline-hanson\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Pauline Hanson</a> did on Wednesday night in our national parliament was a racist and bigoted speech that sought to divide and hurt people. She chose to scapegoat an entire community for the problems some people experience. It was a calculated and shameful speech designed to stoke fear and division in our community.</p>\n<p>Like many Australians, my Greens colleagues and I were bracing for Pauline Hanson\u2019s speech on Wednesday night like never before for a parliamentarian\u2019s first speech. Two decades ago we\u2019d all witnessed the damage words by this same public figure sought to do to people, to whole communities, to a nation. So as this Senator Hanson was preparing to do damage once more, my Greens colleagues and I shared our concerns and discussed what we might do if she crossed a line. </p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-2 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Pauline Hanson calls for immigration ban: 'Go back to where you came from'</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/14/pauline-hanson-first-speech-senate-calls-for-immigration-ban\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>We were guided by the words of Australian of the Year Lieutenant General David Morrison who said that \u201cthe standard you walk past is the standard you accept\u201d.</p>\n<p>Senator Hanson didn\u2019t just cross a line, she deliberately trashed it.</p>\n<p>We chose to walk out of the Senate while Ms Hanson was speaking because we did not want to give any kind of legitimacy to her racist views and to the racist views of others by sitting and listening with the respect usually afforded to parliamentarians during their first speech.</p>\n<p>We believed that as Muslims across the country heard the words and felt the hate directed at them from Pauline Hanson\u2019s speech it was important her message was countered, drowned out if possible, by messages of welcome and respect.</p>\n<p>And we felt an obligation to stand up for not only Muslims but for the millions of Australians who welcome multiculturalism and an Australia that does not judge you on the colour of your skin or your religious beliefs.</p>\n<p>Some have suggested that by walking out we were taking Pauline Hanson seriously and granting her power she did not deserve. But the uncomfortable fact is that Pauline Hanson does have power; she was elected into the parliament, not through preferences but in her own right.</p>\n<p>Senator Hanson has received unprecedented levels of coverage of her racist views, even as a paid commentator by network news. To suggest she could just be allowed to preach hate and fade into the background is ludicrous. And to suggest the Greens elevated the coverage of her second maiden speech is similarly so. The coverage would have been those hateful words beamed into living rooms and personal devices across the globe but with no strong counter message that this is not Australia.</p>\n<p>The 45th Parliament risks being the most divisive parliament in Australia\u2019s history but it doesn\u2019t have to be. Moments like those we saw this week should be used by parliamentarians as opportunities to bring communities together not to divide them. If feedback by the Muslim community is anything to go by I believe we did just that.</p>\n<p>Yesterday as news of the Greens \u201cwalk out\u201d spread the phones in my office began to ring off the hook. In the morning the callers were mainly men who supported Pauline Hanson, angry at what we had done. Then, something remarkable began to happen. Muslims across the country started calling and thanking us. Some had received a text message, others an email or social media post, from their friends and networks, urging people to call.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-2 | 2\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">The most troubling thing about Pauline Hanson's view of Muslims? The facts no longer matter | Susan Carland</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2016/jul/19/the-most-depressing-thing-about-pauline-hansons-view-of-muslims-the-facts-no-longer-matter\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>As the night wore on the calls were in their hundreds and showed no signs of letting up so I sat down with my team to help with the call load. I spoke to one man who told me he had just returned from evening prayers at his mosque where the imam urged the many in attendance to go home and call the Greens and thank us for our stance. We called for reinforcements from my colleague\u2019s offices.</p>\n<p>As I continued to listen to the voices of Muslim Australians, sometimes speaking to multiple people in one family on the one call, I heard why it was so important to them that we did what we did. </p>\n<p>One call in particular resonated with me. A mother told me she was worried about the effect words like those we heard on Wednesday night will have on her children the following day in the schoolyard and on the bus. I told her I understood.</p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "summary": "This could be be the most divisive parliament in Australia\u2019s history. But by standing up to racists, the Greens can help bring communities together"}
{"timestamp": "1474064554000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/17/meeting-pauline-hansons-voters-silent-screamers-find-their-voice", "author": "Bridie Jabour", "title": "Meeting Pauline Hanson's voters: silent screamers find their voice", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><span class=\"drop-cap\"><span class=\"drop-cap__inner\">K</span></span>errie Young\u2019s great yearning in life was to be a rock star. Instead, at 59 years of age, she finds herself as a housewife in Brisbane with two adult children she adores but is confounded by. Her daughter, a Christian convert who is on a scholarship at university, does not \u201cdrink, smoke or have sex\u201d, a puzzled Kerrie says. Her husband thinks Kerrie\u2019s a redneck.</p>\n<p>Young has been a lifelong Labor voter, but at the last election she cast her No 1 Senate vote for Pauline Hanson\u2019s One Nation party. The future terrifies her.</p>\n<p>She is dreadfully nervous about being interviewed as one of the people who voted for Hanson. She speaks quickly at the beginning, looking away and laughing defensively when making certain statements. But she thinks the issue is too important not to speak out about, to try to warn people, to hopefully be at the start of what will become a national conversation.<br/></p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Pauline Hanson is back, and it's still just as hard to counter her rhetoric with facts</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/10/pauline-hanson-is-back-and-its-still-just-as-hard-to-counter-her-rhetoric-with-facts\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>\u201cI don\u2019t think there\u2019s enough awareness of my generation having been told all our lives, paying taxes, paying into superannuation, you can retire, you can get in your bus and travel around, you can go on cruises or whatever, now all of a sudden \u2013 boom \u2013 you can\u2019t. I want to know why,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cMy friend said retirement is not a right, retirement is a privilege and I can\u2019t see that. If we have all paid our taxes, if our parents have paid their taxes, why are we sending the money overseas, why are we bringing in refugees who I read somewhere it cost $60,000 to each set up.</p>\n<p> \u201cThis is my money. This is our money.\u201d</p>\n<p> With her hair in a neat braid, wearing glasses and a simple floral shirt, Young holds forth on all of her fears while sipping a chai latte in a suburban Brisbane shopping centre. Her retirement. Foreign investment. Immigration. Mining destroying arable farming lands. She is one of roughly 134,000 who gave Hanson a first preference vote in Queensland. The hundreds of thousands who cast votes for her One Nation party Australia-wide <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/jul/03/australias-double-dissolution-election-backfires-badly-with-likely-senate-makeup\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">delivered four One Nation representatives into the Senate </a>with the chance to have a powerful influence in a chamber where the government has not got a majority. <strong> <br/></strong></p>\n<p>In the spirit of most dogmatic people <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/10/pauline-hanson-is-back-and-its-still-just-as-hard-to-counter-her-rhetoric-with-facts\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Hanson has not let facts get in the way of her cause</a>. She has <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/video/2016/sep/14/pauline-hanson-australia-in-danger-of-being-swamped-by-muslims-video\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">warned of Australia being swamped by Muslims</a> when they make up 2.2% of the population. In the 1990s Hanson\u2019s focus was on Asians \u2013 so far she has not explained what happened to the supposed invasion of the 1990s. She has linked organised crime, welfare fraud, unemployment and the prison population to Muslims without producing data or evidence to back her claims.</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"83a92c07bd5865ad91dc28681cee0bf64c4a9c1f\" id=\"img-2\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/83a92c07bd5865ad91dc28681cee0bf64c4a9c1f/0_0_4500_3000/4500.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=a9731bb624c74671fa555e24356a239f\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"4500\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3000\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-2\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nPauline Hanson delivers her maiden speech in the Senate on Wednesday. Photograph: Mike Bowers for the Guardian\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>Rising inequality, coupled with the ability to create communities of people who live tens of thousands kilometres apart through social media, has made a fertile patch for Hanson to flourish in.</p>\n<h2>Divided by geography, united by fear</h2>\n<p>Young is a housewife whose husband has dealt with health issues for many years, meaning periods where he has not been able to work.</p>\n<p>Robyn McLaughlin is an amputee recovering from cancer.</p>\n<p>Graham (not his real name) lost his livelihood when he was punched on a night out and acquired a brain injury that meant he was not allowed to work in his manual labour industry anymore.</p>\n<p>Shirley\u2019s daughter looked for work on years after finishing university while Shirley looked on helplessly until one day her daughter suggested they both kill themselves.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">It\u2019s very, very difficult these days to express anything without sounding racist or non-PC</p>\n<footer>\n<cite class=\"pullquote-cite\">Kerrie Young</cite>\n</footer>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>They live scattered across the country, from Western Australia to Newcastle to Townsville, but they all say almost the exact same thing when asked why they voted for Hanson. The economy. They are worried about their futures and terrified for their children\u2019s. Where are they going to live? What jobs are they going to have? How are they going to survive?</p>\n<p>Fuelled by posts on social media, particularly Facebook, they have discovered what they think the root of their problems is \u2013 foreign investment and asset sales. This segues into concern about immigration.</p>\n<p>While Malcolm Turnbull has been talking innovation and Bill Shorten has been pitching to the middle class, those becoming poorer and feeling the class lines shifting under their feet, have had just one person listening to them. They don\u2019t just read Hanson\u2019s Facebook page, they are talking to her. She is talking to them. Hanson responds to multiple comments every day, reassuring people who are upset about particular policies and situations, arguing with people who disagree with her and seemingly taking them into her confidence (\u201cI don\u2019t handle compliments very well\u201d) while her fans tell her they are concerned about immigration, politician wages (\u201ccut them across the board to the average Australian\u2019s wages\u201d) or offering Hanson advice (\u201cI notice you get quite flustered when you are upset or angry, try mindfulness breathing\u201d). </p>\n<p>Or they just talk to her as they would any of their other mates on Facebook. \u201cGood job getting the tea in without looking, really good technique.\u201d</p>\n<p> Young has befriended people as part of the community and has had Hanson respond personally to her messages and comments. Young\u2019s political beliefs are a patchwork that don\u2019t follow the conventional patterns \u2013 she does not really care about marriage equality either way, is passionate about the environment, suspicious of immigration and upset by foreign investment. </p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape element--showcase  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"b232714f6a3896857e79cdb6ef87789b27d044e8\" id=\"img-3\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/b232714f6a3896857e79cdb6ef87789b27d044e8/0_0_4096_2747/4096.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=bf0df9fa07df0b2708bcec7a043b45c1\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"4096\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"2747\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-3\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nPauline Hanson jokingly hides behind one of her campaign signs, surrounded by supporters, during her election-night function in Ipswich, west of Brisbane. Photograph: Dan Peled/EPA\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>She seems slightly surprised at how her life has turned out and will often start ruminating on that while answering questions about policy. At one stage while talking about Indigenous Australians she diverts and reveals she has seen my Facebook profile. \u201cI looked at your wedding photos, you looked so beautiful and happy, I hope you never lose that fresh loveliness, but you will. Nobody gets out of here without a bit of pain.\u201d </p>\n<p>Hanson\u2019s One Nation has been Young\u2019s personal middle ground between parties that have let her down. She will not vote Greens as she does not think they talk about the environment enough and she will not vote Nationals because she thinks they don\u2019t believe in climate change. She has never voted Liberal and she is appalled by Labor\u2019s behaviour over the past six years and does not think there is any talent there anyway.</p>\n<p>\u201cThe rot set in when they all ganged up on Kevin Rudd, everybody I know says Kevin Rudd is a real prick, blah blah blah, if you can\u2019t work with him maybe it\u2019s your problem? Truly brilliant people are really hard to for normal people to deal with, look at Paul Keating. Everyone thought he was an asshole too, but he is brilliant.\u201d</p>\n<p> Young thinks Australia does not have the resources to support many more people and there should be a temporary stop to immigration, as well as an examination of the welfare system. When it comes to these issues, her angst could almost be <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/14/pauline-hanson-first-speech-senate-calls-for-immigration-ban\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">lifted directly from Hanson\u2019s maiden speech</a>.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">All the businesses are gone, car manufacturing is gone, sugar is gone, everything\u2019s gone for that little bit of money</p>\n<footer>\n<cite class=\"pullquote-cite\">Shirley</cite>\n</footer>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p> \u201cThe ones who are working are getting taxed more and more to pay for the people who aren\u2019t working, it\u2019s just untenable, it\u2019s not possible to keep going that way. It\u2019s like if you get a fish tank and they\u2019ve got too many fish in it, they start eating each other. That\u2019s what happens,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cIt\u2019s very, very difficult these days to express anything without sounding racist or non-PC. I wouldn\u2019t hurt anybody, I don\u2019t care what you do in your own time, I honestly believe there is a section out there who stop any intelligent debate by throwing these \u2018vile racist bigot\u2019 comments around. Is there a way to express disapproval of certain value systems and certain belief systems without sounding racist? Is there a way of doing it? Or do you just have to wear it? I\u2019ve been called that, my friend that I walk with every day calls me her redneck friend. And I say to her \u2018are you aware that this happens in Islam? Do you understand what Eid is?\u2019\u201d</p>\n<h2>The cause that dare not speak its name</h2>\n<p> Young is also called a redneck by her husband and the mocking by people close to her is common to other Hanson voters. Further north on the Sunshine Coast Shirley talks in a granny flat she is housesitting. </p>\n<p> Shirley\u2019s daughter does not know that she votes Hanson (\u201cI would never tell her, she supports Muslims\u201d) and Shirley is careful before she tells friends, sounding them out first to see if they already agree with her on other issues.</p>\n<p> As she welcomes me at the door she tells me she has been researching my name and knows it is Lebanese. \u201cIs your father a Muslim?\u201d she asks narrowing her eyes. To her small comfort the family were Maronite Christian when they arrived in Australia.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 2\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Pauline Hanson emerges as the queen of a potentially unruly Senate | Katharine Murphy</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/aug/04/pauline-hanson-emerges-as-the-queen-of-a-potentially-unruly-senate\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p> \u201c[Hanson is] interested in what I\u2019m interested in which is the selling of Australia, I don\u2019t mind foreign investment but our land is going, if you go to another country you can\u2019t buy the land \u2026 Australia is just too open,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p>A short and talkative woman who cheerfully describes herself as fat, Shirley is 66 and retired. She has lived in Cairns and Sydney before settling on the Sunshine Coast and voted Labor until she switched to One Nation at the last election. She is also a Sri Lankan immigrant.</p>\n<p> \u201cI got out of Sydney because people thought I was Muslim, and I get Muslim men looking at me, I started to feel treated differently, in shops people weren\u2019t serving me,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cI got this in Cairns in the 70s \u2026 I remember getting an ice cream for my little girl, who\u2019s really white, can\u2019t go in the sun \u2026 they could see me, it was packed this ice cream shop, all these people were behind me, these girls were serving everyone in the shop except for me. </p>\n<p>\u201cI got really sick of it, I said really loud \u2018Am I too short? Am I too black for you to serve me?\u2019 It happened so many times in Cairns, it really did. We were classed as Aboriginal, we were treated as Aboriginal, which was not very nice. </p>\n<p> \u201cThere\u2019s still racism here, I feel it I know it and I don\u2019t care.\u201d</p>\n<p> So does she have any empathy for how Muslim people, and Aboriginal people, may feel about Hanson and her comments? She concedes Hanson \u201ccame across as racist\u201d in the 1990s in the way she spoke about Aboriginal people but what Hanson really wanted was equality for all, not for one group (Indigenous people) to be treated differently from other Australians by getting certain welfare payments.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">It\u2019s about time Australians stood ground for their own country</p>\n<footer>\n<cite class=\"pullquote-cite\">Graham</cite>\n</footer>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>\u201cShe said you\u2019re gonna lose Australia, Australia is going to be lost, and all these yeas later she\u2019s absolutely right, we\u2019re selling Australia. It\u2019s OK to have foreign investments, but all the businesses are gone, car manufacturing is gone, sugar is gone, everything\u2019s gone for that little bit of money, they\u2019ve sold it,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> \u201cThey\u2019re sending everything offshore where it\u2019s cheaper, so it\u2019s not Australians getting employed, the mining, they\u2019re employing people on 457 visas, I think it\u2019s the worst thing ever, that loophole.\u201d</p>\n<p> Shirley\u2019s primary concern is foreign investment but while others want to ban all immigration as an extension of that, or loathe Muslims, she is more tepid. She tells a story of being glared at by a woman in a headscarf to illustrate her point about some of them not being trustworthy.</p>\n<p>\u201cStop the people from coming at the moment, but they\u2019re not all bad, I know some good ones, and they agree, because they say \u2018we don\u2019t know who\u2019s coming in\u2019, they consider themselves Australian. They don\u2019t want sharia law, these are Muslims talking to me, the average Australian does not want it, they\u2019re too scared to say anything,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p>\u201cI\u2019m not a politician, I\u2019m not an accountant, I\u2019m not anybody who knows anything but I see stuff and think \u2018that doesn\u2019t look right to me\u2019, the average Joe Blow feels things more than they actually understand or know, they feel things, they know stuff.\u201d </p>\n<h2>Hardship, hard yards and grievance unheeded</h2>\n<p>Most of Hanson\u2019s supporters do just \u201cknow stuff\u201d. A lot of their news, like most people\u2019s, comes from Facebook. But theirs is dissected by rightwing blogs and sites. Their world view is reinforced on pages such as Hanson\u2019s and their own invitation-only private groups with more than 10,000 people congregating on one.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 3\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Comprehending Pauline is not the challenge. Engaging constructively with Hansonism is | Katharine Murphy</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2016/sep/14/comprehending-pauline-is-not-the-challenge-engaging-constructively-with-hansonism-is\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p> They are mostly older than 50, mostly live in regional areas, and have not had easy lives. Their grievances, real and imagined, make up the bedrock of their politics. For a long time they have not felt voiceless, but that they have been screaming and nobody is listening to them.</p>\n<p>They are driven by their own circumstance, the greater good and other people do not really factor into it. It\u2019s about what they have lost, what\u2019s slipped through their fingers, what their children are going to miss out on. They don\u2019t have the luxury of worrying about other people.</p>\n<p> In Newcastle, Robyn McLaughlin is recovering from chemotherapy after being diagnosed with cancer while getting treatment related to her amputated right leg. She has long been faithful to the minor parties and voted for Hanson in the 1990s, for much the same reasons that she votes for her now.</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"dc2909c189a38e78ac09506306d4e250c0b865ff\" id=\"img-4\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/dc2909c189a38e78ac09506306d4e250c0b865ff/0_0_5376_3024/5376.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=e6c70321a02af50eea91d0826c317cea\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"5376\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3024\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-4\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nHanson speaks at a rally against Islam in Brisbane in April 2015. Photograph: Jamie McKinnell/AAP\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p> \u201cBringing all these so-called refugees into the country there\u2019s no infrastructure to support what we\u2019ve got here, it\u2019s already been drained. I\u2019m a baby boomer, I\u2019ve worked all my life, I\u2019ve done the hard yards, I\u2019ve paid taxes and yet because I\u2019ve saved money and been taught to be sensible for a rainy day I can\u2019t even get a disability pension, it\u2019s quite unfair. Myself aside, there\u2019s pensioners, veterans, kids on street and all this is being ignored and we\u2019re bringing in all these people, they don\u2019t want to integrate,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p> The 67-year-old is a dyed-in-the-wool Hanson supporter who she says she pays extra to go to a butcher that uses a halal free abattoir and that the Trans-Pacific Partnership agreement \u201cfits nicely into the global governance that the UN is pushing\u201d.</p>\n<p> Graham is another who, having taken body blow after body blow throughout his life, is easily convinced of the existence of villains and Hanson is happy to supply them. Graham suffered an acquired brain injury after being punched in 2001 and though he has recovered his speech and motor skills he is not allowed to work in the maritime industry. After, as he puts it, being followed by the black dog for a number of years, he is rebuilding his life in Western Australia. But he is worried. He is worried about how he is going to keep finding work, he is worried about his daughters on the other side of the country in Victoria, he is worried he could get hit again, he is worried about what could happen next, and he is worried about Muslims.</p>\n<p> \u201cPrimary schools are going visiting mosques, that\u2019s trying to encourage kids and speaking about their religion, and then when you see their side of Islam and what they do actually believe in is pretty disgusting. They turned their religion into a violent religion. It\u2019s about time Australians stood ground for their own country, my grandfather and great uncles didn\u2019t go to war to let other societies into our country to change our religion and the way we live our free life.</p>\n<p> \u201cI worry about my kids and their kids, putting all these mosques around Australia. All of a sudden they will be putting their votes in and they won\u2019t allow our Anzacs to sell or pledge their poppies or raise concerns.\u201d </p>\n<p> Graham is strident in his political beliefs but does not want his full name printed like many other Hanson supporters. They say they don\u2019t feel ashamed voting for Hanson but most have people very close to them who do not know how they vote.</p>\n<p> They see the election of Hanson as a final stand, one of their very last chances to be heard, a slight possibility that maybe the future will be OK. They feel Hanson understands them, and to many Hanson voters, what they feel is crucial.</p>\n<p>Back in the suburban shopping centre Young sighs and looks past the shoulder of the person sitting next to her when she talks about the reaction to her choice to vote for Hanson.</p>\n<p>\u201cPeople immediately, many people, the minute you mention <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/pauline-hanson\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Pauline Hanson</a> roll their eyes and call her a racist or a yobbo, or that stupid woman \u2026 she\u2019s xenophobic.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-4 | 4\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Pauline Hanson's maiden speech to the Australian Senate \u2013 full text</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/pauline-hansons-maiden-speech-to-the-australian-senate-full-text\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>\u201cNo, she\u2019s someone who feels something [but] who wasn\u2019t educated enough to know the big words, that\u2019s all. I really believe her heart is in the right place and what she\u2019s trying to say, is very, very pertinent to how we should be thinking bout the future but it\u2019s just so much easier to call her a racist bigot rather than actually think about something and do something about something that is going to affect you and your children.\u201d</p>\n<p>Hanson\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/politicians-and-muslim-leaders-condemn-hanson-she-doesnt-know-what-shes-talking-about\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">views are inflammatory</a>, divisive and simplistic. But while her supporters\u2019 views can be out of step with mainstream Australia, they constitute a growing minority that needs to be acknowledged. Labor and Liberal parties have had falling primary votes since the early 1990s and at the most recent election One Nation recorded a higher primary vote in Queensland than the Greens. Just <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/politicians-and-muslim-leaders-condemn-hanson-she-doesnt-know-what-shes-talking-about\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">condemning Hanson</a> is not enough; there is an argument to be properly explained and won. The people who vote for Hanson, mostly from increasingly marginalised communities, are ignored at the country\u2019s peril. </p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "summary": "Bridie Jabour travels in search of the people who brought One Nation back into parliament, scattered across the country and with a variety of experiences but with real and imagined grievances at the bedrock of their politics"}

{"timestamp": "1474063194000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/17/un-human-rights-office-calls-on-australia-to-end-offshore-detention", "author": "Paul Farrell", "title": "UN human rights office calls on Australia to end offshore detention", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>Australia must show \u201cpolitical courage\u201d and end the indefinite detention of asylum seekers held on <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/nauru\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Nauru</a>, the new Pacific representative of the United Nation human rights office of the high commissioner has said.</p>\n<p>In an interview with Guardian Australia Chitralekha Massey, spoke at length about Australia\u2019s offshore detention policies. </p>\n<p>She said Australia\u2019s detention of asylum seekers on Nauru \u201cis unsustainable, it\u2019s a violation and it\u2019s unnecessary\u201d. The continuing reports of abuse, self-harm and sexual assault had created an alarming environment at the centre that Massey said needed be resolved.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/aug/10/the-nauru-files-2000-leaked-reports-reveal-scale-of-abuse-of-children-in-australian-offshore-detention\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">The Guardian\u2019s publication of the Nauru files</a> has put the treatment and conditions of asylum seekers held on the Pacific island back into the spotlight. </p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-2 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Asylum-seeker processing at Nauru will 'continue for decades', says Dutton</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/asylum-seeker-processing-at-nauru-will-continue-for-decades-says-dutton\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>Massey said that the asylum seekers held on Nauru had to be given the opportunity to resettle in Australia or another country if they had been found to be refugees. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/unitednations\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">United Nations</a> general assembly and a key migration summit hosted by the United States president, Barack Obama, will be held next week. The Australian prime minister, Malcolm Turnbull, and the immigration minister, Peter Dutton, will be both be in attendance.</p>\n<p>Massey encouraged the Australian government to bring an end to the detention of men, woman and children on Nauru, where hundreds of asylum seekers languished in \u201cnot only prolonged, but indefinite\u201d detention.</p>\n<p>Massey\u2019s team completed an inspection of the Nauru centre in August 2016. She said the situation in the past two years had been \u201caggravated even further\u201d, based on the observations of her office\u2019s latest visit.</p>\n<p>\u201cWe have repeatedly reported our concerns around healthcare, around education, access to justice,\u201d she said.</p>\n<p>\u201cWe are particularly concerned about the sexual violence and the number of rapes against women, against children. The amount of self-harm that is really an indicator of how bad the mental health of people has deteriorated.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s difficult for me to find words to describe how somebody can go from being at a breaking point and just continue to be at a breaking point endlessly.</p>\n<p>\u201cThere is an urgent response required.\u201d</p>\n<p>In response to Dutton\u2019s comments that Australia\u2019s regional processing relationship with Nauru would continue for \u201cdecades\u201d she said: \u201cIt\u2019s already unacceptable.\u201d </p>\n<p>She urged Australia to adopt a \u201cnon-custodial\u201d approach to migration and those seeking asylum: \u201cThere is a better way to do this.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s very important that the children on Nauru receive, with urgency, the chance for normal lives.\u201d</p>\n<p>She said she looked favourably at <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/14/australias-refugee-impasse-rights-commission-suggests-ways-forward\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">the Australian Human Rights Commission\u2019s recent report</a> Pathways to Protection, which canvassed a number of options to encourage a more humane and regional response from Australia.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-2 | 2\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Peter Dutton open to refugees on Nauru being resettled in New Zealand</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/peter-dutton-open-to-refugees-on-nauru-being-resettled-in-new-zealand\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>She also noted that while the detention centre on Nauru moved to an \u201copen centre\u201d arrangement in October 2015, asylum seekers held on the island still lived in \u201cmilitarised, police-like\u201d arrangements. She also urged Australia to take up a greater regional role in bolstering the human rights framework of neighbouring Pacific countries.</p>\n<p>The UN office continues to focus on other aspects of Australia\u2019s approach to human rights.
