{"timestamp": "1474007236000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/artanddesign/2016/sep/16/vincent-van-gough-exhibition-headlines-national-gallery-of-victoria-2017-program", "author": "Steph Harmon", "title": "Vincent van Gogh exhibition headlines National Gallery of Victoria 2017 program", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>More than 60 artworks by Vincent van Gogh will be coming to the National Gallery of Victoria (NGV) in 2017, many of which have never been shown in Australia. </p>\n<p>The world premiere exhibition, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/artanddesign/van-gogh\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Van Gogh</a> and the Seasons, will be next year\u2019s instalment of the NGV\u2019s Winter Masterpieces series, comprised of 40 paintings and 25 drawings.</p>\n<p>Announced on Friday, the exhibition will be presented in four sections, devoted to each season, under the curation of art historian Sjraar van Heugten, former head of collections at the Van Gogh Museum. Works from van Gogh\u2019s own art collection will be included, along with additional documentary material.</p>\n<p>Tony Ellwood, director of the NGV, described it as a \u201ctrue coup\u201d for the gallery. </p>\n<p>\u201cVan Gogh was a true original. His love of the seasons was deeply profound and played an important role in his life and practice. This reverence for summer, autumn, winter and spring and the eternal cycles of nature is seen in the energy and dynamism of his distinct brushstrokes, which almost leap off the canvas with vitality.\u201d</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape element--supporting  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"d47a49ca454dcff593ee10a158f40526b2cede35\" id=\"img-2\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/d47a49ca454dcff593ee10a158f40526b2cede35/0_0_3000_2071/3000.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=69de1eae01dfaf27f540a5338fa3a01e\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"3000\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"2071\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-2\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nThe Great Wave by Japanese ukiyo-e artist Katsushika Hokusai. Photograph: NGV International\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>The announcement was made as the gallery\u2019s 2017 autumn/winter program was announced, including the most comprehensive exhibition of work by Katsushika Hokusai, the founding father of manga, seen in Australia. </p>\n<p>Opening in July 2017 and featuring 129 prints, four paintings and 10 rare books on loan from Japan\u2019s Ukiyo-e Museum in Matsumoto, the self-titled exhibition will be accompanied by a selection of Hokusai works from the NGV Collection, including his most famous image, A Great Wave.</p>\n<p>The NGV also announced Festival of Photography, which will take place in March across 11 gallery spaces and feature work by Bill Henson, Zo\u00eb Croggon and Patrick Pound, as well as William Eggleston Portraits, an Australian exclusive exhibition of the American photographer\u2019s work, which is <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/artanddesign/2016/jul/24/william-eggleston-portraits-review-national-portrait-gallery\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">currently showing</a> at the National Portrait Gallery in London.</p>\n<p>In December, NGV Australia will exhibit the work of a broad range of Indigenous artists in a group show, Who\u2019s Afraid Of Colour? With an in-depth focus on major female artists, including Julie Gough, Destiny Deacon, Emily Kam Kngwarray, Queenie McKenzie and Nonggirrnga Marawili, it will feature \u201cbold statements that explore colour and assert the politics of identity\u201d.</p>\n<p><em><span class=\"bullet\">\u2022</span> Van Gogh and the Seasons opens at NGV International on 28 April</em></p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "summary": "More than 60 van Gogh artworks, many never shown in Australia before, are the centrepiece of an NGV autumn/winter program that also features Katsushika Hokusai and Festival of Photography"}
{"timestamp": "1474085221000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/17/julie-bishop-says-australia-will-look-elsewhere-if-us-doesnt-pass-trade-deal", "author": "Melissa Davey", "title": "Julie Bishop says Australia will look elsewhere if US doesn't pass trade deal", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>Australia will seek out alternative free trade agreements in the region should the Trans-Pacific Partnership fail to pass a US Congress vote, the foreign affairs minister, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/julie-bishop\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Julie Bishop</a>, has said.</p>\n<p>Bishop made the comments while addressing reporters in Washington, where she has met representatives for US presidential candidates Hillary Clinton and Donald Trump. She will also meet the US Secretary of State, John Kerry, and attend US president Barack Obama\u2019s leaders\u2019 summit on refugees in New York.</p>\n<p>Clinton and Trump oppose the 12-country Trans-Pacific Partnership, saying the deal is not in the US interest. However Obama is committed to passing the agreement through the Congress and Senate before his term ends.</p>\n<p>Bishop said she had urged the Trump and Clinton camps to view the deal as \u201cnot only economically important but strategically vital for our region\u201d.</p>\n<p>\u201cI had a fairly sympathetic hearing from all of the representatives who see that free trade is the basis of US economic success,\u201d she said.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-2 | Productivity Commission</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" {"timestamp": "1474079531000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/17/stephen-conroy-informed-bill-shorten-about-resignation-by-text-message", "author": "Melissa Davey", "title": "Stephen Conroy informed Bill Shorten about resignation by text message", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>The opposition leader, Bill Shorten, has made his first public comments on the <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/16/stephen-conroy-resigns-from-the-senate\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">shock resignation of Labor\u2019s deputy Senate leader, Stephen Conroy</a>, telling reporters in Washington that Conroy informed him he was going to resign via text message.</p>\n<p>Conroy, who held the communications portfolio, was one of Shorten\u2019s most valuable factional allies and also served under the former prime ministers Kevin Rudd and Julia Gillard.<br/></p>\n<p>Shorten is in Washington to meet with US officials following a meeting last week with Canadian leader Justin Trudeau in Montreal. On Saturday he told reporters that Conroy had attempted to contact him by text before tabling his resignation.</p>\n<p>\u201cSenator Conroy endeavoured to contact me, by text, different time zones in Canada,\u201d Shorten said. </p>\n<p>\u201cHe then made his statement.\u201d</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-2 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">The Conroy conundrum: enforcer's departure leaves Bill Shorten exposed</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/16/the-conroy-conundrum-enforcers-departure-leaves-bill-shorten-exposed\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>Shorten he said he had no criticisms of his colleague, saying the senator had chosen to put his family first.</p>\n<p>\u201cI am not going to criticise him for that,\u201d Shorten said. </p>\n<p>\u201cStephen Conroy has served the Australian Senate and the <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/labor-party\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Labor party</a> and the Australian people with fearless energy and great passion for 20 years. I only wish him, his wife and daughter the very best in the future.</p>\n<p>\u201cHe has chosen to prioritise his family over a future engagement in politics after two decades, he steps down with the best wishes and the blessings of the Labor party.\u201d </p>\n<p>He said the party was still in the process of finding a replacement, with the government confirming it intends to grant Labor a pair until Conroy can be replaced.</p>\n<p>During the news conference, Shorten was again asked whether he would tell the Labor caucus to block the same-sex marriage plebiscite. {"timestamp": "1474092041000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/technology/2016/sep/17/airbnb-nuisance-neighbours-tribunal-ruling", "author": "Lara Williams", "title": "When Airbnb rentals become nuisance neighbours", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><span class=\"drop-cap\"><span class=\"drop-cap__inner\">I</span></span> first realised I was living next door to a weekend sublet two years ago. Late one Saturday night I heard boys yelling and loud music, and the thumping against the walls was so hard one of my picture frames fell off and cracked on the floor. I presumed the neighbours had a teenager who was throwing a cheeky party while their parents were away. When it happened again the following weekend I assumed it was a repeat. However, a few weekends later it was girls yelling, playing what I recognised to be the true hymn of the hen party, You Can Leave Your Hat On. Suddenly it made sense: I was living next door to a sublet playing host to hen parties and stag dos most weekends.</p>\n<p>I\u2019ve had men wrestling on the floor outside my flat, someone trying to kick in my door, and fights that have left blood smears across the corridor walls. I\u2019d refrained from complaining to the building manager or letting agents and tried to deal with the host directly.</p>\n<p>I had nothing against someone trying to make a little extra cash over the weekend. It was when it became clear the property was being entirely used for short-term rentals, and after my second phone call to the police, that I started complaining. I complained to the building manager, to my landlord, to the council. So far, nothing has been done.</p>\n<p>Weekend sublets such as those offered on <a href=\"http://www.airbnb.co.uk/\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Airbnb</a> and <a href=\"http://www.booking.com/\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Booking.com</a> have revolutionised holidays. But I\u2019m not the only person to have a bad experience. Paul, a teacher with a flat in Edinburgh, noticed people trundling by his apartment with luggage. Then he was kept awake by late-night noise. \u201cThe irritation was that it was very difficult to get in touch with the owner via the Airbnb website. I had to pretend to be interested in renting it in order to send them a message,\u201d he says, and he claims that \u201cthe problems have left people in negative equity\u201d.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">Residents alleged that the Airbnb host had breached several terms in his lease agreement, and the tribunal judge agreed</p>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>If you want to hear a real <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/technology/airbnb\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Airbnb</a> horror story, how about the one involving the riot police who were called to a flat in Brixton, south London, after 150 people arrived for a party that turned into chaos? In that case, reported in the Times in May, residents had apparently called the police on several occasions to break up parties in the flat, which had been let through the website. One complained that a partygoer \u201clanded with a crash on to his balcony from above\u201d and knocked on his window to get back in.</p>\n<p>In the First-Tier Tribunal (Property Chamber), which handles disputes over property and land, the residents alleged that the Airbnb host had breached several terms in his lease agreement, and the tribunal judge agreed, saying the defendant appeared to be using the property as a guesthouse. It\u2019s the first known ruling against an Airbnb host by the tribunal \u2013 but probably won\u2019t be the last.</p>\n<p>Plenty more alarming tales can be found on <a href=\"http://www.airbnbhell.com/\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">AirbnbHell.com</a>, a website \u201cdedicated to helping hosts and guests share their stories about the risks and dangers of using Airbnb\u201d.</p>\n<p>Cal King, shows editor at TV channel Comedy Central, rents a flat in London next door to one that is empty quite a lot of the time, \u201cand then each weekend a different group of raucous people turn up and have parties\u201d. He is sanguine. \u201cIn a way, I quite like knowing that even though there\u2019s pounding tropical house at 1am, chances are they\u2019ll be gone tomorrow.\u201d</p>\n<p>Katie Gray, a barrister at Tanfield Chambers, says that in the first instance you should see if there can be anything done informally, for example by having a conversation with tenants or the host directly. If this does not work, she suggests you gather as much evidence as possible. \u201cKeep a diary of events, record the frequency of the lettings, and the dates and times of the nuisance.\u201d</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"a2216ac225eba2dc88c86a18be964f26e4ba9dde\" id=\"img-2\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/a2216ac225eba2dc88c86a18be964f26e4ba9dde/0_202_6016_3612/6016.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=b1f511d6b91ed195f93fe45b6793e4f8\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"6016\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3612\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-2\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nThe legal avenues available to resolve disputes will depend on whether the property is leasehold or freehold. Photograph: John Macdougall/AFP/Getty Images\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>The legal avenues available, should it come to this, will depend on whether the property is leasehold or freehold. For leasehold properties, owners or tenants will have to report the issue to the freeholder of the block, who will be the people able to take action.</p>\n<p>In terms of longer nuisance sublets, local authorities may offer protection. For example, in London, stays longer than 90 days require previous planning permission.</p>\n<p>If you are selling your property, things become a little tricky. You are required to complete a property information form disclosing any disputes or complaints about the properties or properties nearby. If you have been in a dispute about an Airbnb letting and you do not inform the buyer, you could be liable in court for misrepresentation and potentially be asked to pay damages to the buyer. In an extreme situation the sale will not go through.</p>\n<p>Airbnb now has well over 1m properties and is active in 200 countries. One of the key features of the website is the review function: guests can review the properties they have stayed in, and hosts can review their guests. Though neighbours have, until recently, been left out in the cold.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">New York laws ban apartments in buildings with three or more units from being rented out for less than 30 days</p>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>Two weeks after the Brixton case emerged and was widely publicised, Airbnb <a href=\"http://blog.airbnb.com/new-resource-for-neighbors/\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">launched an online tool</a> for neighbours of its hosts who experience problems and want to make a complaint. The site reviews whether your complaint matches up with an active Airbnb listing, then messages the host. If problems persist, the website says it can suspend or remove them from Airbnb entirely. However, it is not clear if anyone has yet been banned. Airbnb says just one in 18,000 UK guest arrivals has prompted a complaint via the tool.</p>\n<p>\u201cThe overwhelming majority of Airbnb hosts and guests are good neighbours and respectful travellers,\u201d the company says. \u201cWe want to do everything we can to help our community members be good neighbours.\u201d</p>\n<p>In a recent blog, it pledged to treat each case seriously. \u201cHosting is a big responsibility,\u201d it said, \u201cand those who repeatedly fail to meet our standards and expectations will be subject to suspension or removal from the Airbnb community.\u201d</p>\n<h2>The cities cracking down on Airbnb<br/></h2>\n<p>The idea of Airbnb and other short-term lets as an alternative to over-priced hotels may soon be over, <em>writes Patrick Collinson</em>. Many cities have begun to introduce new rules, after residents complained about being overwhelmed by weekend visitors banging wheelie bags up stairs, breaching building security rules, and loud parties. Pressure has also come from hotel groups and local politicians who have lost revenue from hotel taxes. </p>\n<p><strong>Berlin</strong><br/>In June, a court upheld Berlin\u2019s de facto ban on short-term rentals. People who let more than 50% of their apartment on a short-term basis without a permit risk a fine of \u20ac100,000 (\u00a385,000). City authorities were concerned that the availability of affordable housing was being severely threatened by the rise of short-term letting. Munich and Hamburg have also taken steps to curb <br/>short-term lets. </p>\n<p><strong>San Francisco </strong><br/>The city that is home to Airbnb\u2019s HQ is also one of its fiercest opponents. Hosts have to register with the authorities; if Airbnb advertises an un\u00adregistered property it can be fined $1,000 (\u00a3755) a day for each listing. An action group in the city has posted \u201cwanted\u201d flyers. The crime? \u201cAirbnb\u2019ing our community\u201d and \u201cdestroying affordable housing for immigrant, minority, and low income families\u201d. <br/></p>\n<p><strong>New York</strong> <br/>The city\u2019s rental laws ban apartments in buildings with three or more units from being rented out for less than 30 days. Landlords who flout the ban can be fined as much as $7,500. But home \u00adsharing \u2013 where the host is \u00adpresent \u2013 is legal. Critics say that short-term rental companies like Airbnb are \u00adflooding the city\u2019s housing \u00admarket, reducing available housing stock citywide by 10%, \u00adaccording to a study released in June. <br/></p>\n<p><strong>Barcelona</strong></p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"9ca17518f67a6ead3c680c855818d6b1e16cc792\" id=\"img-3\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/9ca17518f67a6ead3c680c855818d6b1e16cc792/0_399_5928_3558/5928.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=d7daf720e58e98c66f3b94f85b5f4aa2\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"5928\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3558\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-3\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nBarcelona is popular for Airbnb rentals. Photograph: kiko_jimenez/Getty Images/iStockphoto\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>The Catalan city has been among the most aggressive in fighting Airbnb, \u00adslapping a \u20ac30,000 fine on the site for hosting illegal tourist lets in 2014. Flat owners have to list their apartments with the city\u2019s tourism register, obtain a licence and be responsible for collecting the daily \u20ac0.65 tourist tax. </p>\n<p><strong>Madrid</strong><br/>The Spanish capital set a minimum stay of five nights in private homes and apartments which, given the \u00adtypical three-night stay on Airbnb, ruled out most rentals. But the directive was later \u00adoverturned in court. </p>\n<p><strong>Reykjavik </strong><br/>The 1,600 short-term lets in Iceland\u2019s capital have to operate under strict rules introduced in June. The legislation limits the number of days residents can offer rentals in their properties to 90 days a year before they must pay \u00adbusiness tax.<br/></p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "summary": "Short-term sublets can turn into a nightmare, but a tribunal ruling offers some hope to long-suffering residents"}
{"timestamp": "1474064148000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/business/grogonomics/2016/sep/17/jobless-rate-offers-coalition-a-chance-to-brag-so-why-has-it-barely-had-a-mention", "author": "Greg Jericho", "title": "Jobless rate offers Coalition a chance to brag, so why has it barely had a mention?", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/malcolm-turnbull\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Malcolm Turnbull</a> and Scott Morrison got a nice first-year anniversary present this week when Australia recorded its best unemployment rate for three years. Oddly however, they both ignored the news and preferred to talk about the deal they made with Liberal party room on superannuation.</p>\n<p>When the ABS announced that the seasonally adjusted unemployment rate of 5.6%, the lowest since July 2013 \u2013 that is at any time during the Abbott/Turnbull period of government \u2013 you would have expected the boasting to have been long and loud.</p>\n<p>And yet there was mostly silence.</p>\n<p>The employment minister <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/michaelia-cash\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Michaelia Cash</a> gave a brief press conference, and during Senate question time after questions from her own side on superannuation, defence, innovation and science she was asked about the figures \u2013 not exactly it a high priority.</p>\n<p>Anyone who tuned into the House of Representatives question time, however, would have found nothing to enlighten them on the current state of the labour market. The prime minister was even given a nice broad question about the government\u2019s \u201ccommitment to deliver economic security for Australians\u201d. </p>\n<p>In his response, the closest he came to talking of the figures was to note that \u201cjobs are growing\u201d. </p>\n<p>That at least was closer than the treasurer came to mentioning the good figures. All Morrison wanted to talk about was the changes to the superannuation system. </p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-1 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Australia's unemployment rate reaches lowest level in three years</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2016/sep/15/australias-unemployment-rate-reaches-lowest-level-in-three-years\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>The closest anyone came to talking about the actual situation of jobs was Christopher Pyne <a href=\"http://parlinfo.aph.gov.au/parlInfo/search/display/display.w3p;query=Id%3A%22chamber%2Fhansardr%2F9de5f081-9ccf-4f72-a05a-02462c1f3a0c%2F0114%22\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">who told parliament</a> that \u201cwe created over 200,000 jobs in the last 12 months\u201d (it was actually 191,000 in trend terms or 180,000 in seasonally adjusted, so not quite 200,000 let alone \u201cover\u201d). </p>\n<p>In both houses the big issue was the changes to superannuation. </p>\n<p>The lack of attention on actual unemployment highlights the triumph of the \u201cbudget is the economy\u201d argument, where anything that reduces the budget deficit is considered an inherent good. </p>\n<p>It also highlights that despite the impressive overall unemployment rate, the employment situation is not that good.</p>\n<p>Malcolm Turnbull suggested that \u201cjobs are growing\u201d, but mostly it is part-time jobs that are growing and even overall job growth is slowing dramatically.</p>\n<p>Last year in the first eight months 191,000 jobs were created; this year it is just 83,900. The situation for full-time work is particularly bad \u2013 there are now 21,000 fewer full-time jobs than there were in December. </p>\n<p>And August also saw a record set for the level of underemployed workers. </p>\n<p>So it is no surprise really that the government was happy to focus on superannuation reforms which reduce the budget deficit. </p>\n<p>And what was the upshot of these reforms? </p>\n<p>The prime minister noted that 96% of people would be better off or unaffected. Among of those who will \u201cbenefit\u201d are low-income earners who will profit from the government replacing the \u201c<a href=\"https://www.ato.gov.au/Individuals/Super/In-detail/Growing/Low-income-super-contribution/\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">low income super contribution</a>,\u201d which is worth up to $500 a year with the \u201c<a href=\"https://www.ato.gov.au/General/New-legislation/In-detail/Super/Introducing-a-Low-Income-Superannuation-Tax-Offset/\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">low income superannuation tax offset</a>,\u201d which is worth up to ... err ... $500 a year.</p>\n<p>And just how adversely affected the remaining 4% will be is up for debate. </p>\n<p>The high-income-earner-friendly Australian Financial Review headlined an article on the policy with \u201cWealthy are the winners in Coalition\u2019s superannuation deal\u201d. It also led another article explaining what the \u201cchanges mean for you\u201d by noting that \u201cwealthy savers were granted a last chance to stash up to $540,000 from after-tax earnings before the end of the financial year\u201d.</p>\n<p>So you would be right in wondering just how big a hair cut the very wealthy will be having. </p>\n<p>It\u2019s worth noting that the savings to the budget are estimated to be roughly $3bn over the next four years. That sounds big until you realise Treasury estimates the amount of revenue foregone through superannuation tax concessions is around $140bn over that same period. </p>\n<p>And the changes to the policy \u2013 which among other things saw a backflip on the proposal to impose a $500,000 lifetime limit on post-tax contributions \u2013 was not arrived at though some great bipartisan negotiation. The negotiation was all within the Liberal party room and effectively involved giving the disgruntled and very emboldened rightwing of the party room what it wanted. </p>\n<p>The ALP will pass the changes \u2013 there is no reason not to \u2013 and there will be many a story about backflips or good deal-making, and others about how the government is at least making steps to improve the budget, and how important and good that is. </p>\n<p>The government for the most part will welcome such stories \u2013 for they will spin the narrative as best they can. And better those stories than focussing on how for the employment situation looks a lots less buoyant than it was 12 months ago when Turnbull took office.</p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "summary": "At 5.6% Australia\u2019s unemployment rate is at its lowest in three years, but true jobs market picture doesn\u2019t fit the government\u2019s economic narrative"}

But they are penalised for not releasing and Foley just needs to kick it out to finish the game.</p>\n<p>So he does just that.</p>\n</div>\n\n<p class=\"block-share--liveblog-mobile\" data-open-overlay-on-click=\"share-modal-block-57dd3121e4b0df02df203297\" data-link-name=\"open mobile block share\">\n<button class=\"block-share__item--mobile button button--small button--tertiary mobile-only\">\nShare\n</button>\n</p>\n\n</div>\n<div id=\"block-57dd30cbe4b0df02df203294\" class=\"block block--content\" itemprop=\"liveBlogUpdate\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/BlogPosting\">\n<p class=\"block-time published-time\">\n<a href=\"/sport/live/2016/sep/17/rugby-championship-australia-v-argentina-live?page=with:block-57dd30cbe4b0df02df203294#block-57dd30cbe4b0df02df203294\" itemprop=\"url\" class=\"block-time__link\">\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T12:03:38.000Z\" data-relativeformat=\"med\" class=\" js-timestamp\" itemprop=\"datePublished\">10.03pm <span class=\"timezone\">AEST</span></time>\n<span class=\"block-time__absolute\">22:03</span>\n</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"block-elements block-elements--no-byline\" itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n<p><strong>79 min:</strong> Another scrum and we\u2019re just waiting for the final siren now. Yet they\u2019re 16 behind. </p>\n</div>\n\n<p class=\"block-share--liveblog-mobile\" data-open-overlay-on-click=\"share-modal-block-57dd3025e4b0c762d480d5f9\" data-link-name=\"open mobile block share\">\n<button class=\"block-share__item--mobile button button--small button--tertiary mobile-only\">\nShare\n</button>\n</p>\n\n</div>\n<div id=\"block-57dd2fdae4b0df02df203290\" class=\"block block--content is-key-event\" itemprop=\"liveBlogUpdate\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/BlogPosting\">\n<p class=\"block-time published-time\">\n<a href=\"/sport/live/2016/sep/17/rugby-championship-australia-v-argentina-live?page=with:block-57dd2fdae4b0df02df203290#block-57dd2fdae4b0df02df203290\" itemprop=\"url\" class=\"block-time__link\">\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T11:59:11.000Z\" data-relativeformat=\"med\" class=\" js-timestamp\" itemprop=\"datePublished\">9.59pm <span class=\"timezone\">AEST</span></time>\n<span class=\"block-time__absolute\">21:59</span>\n</a>\n</p>\n<h2 class=\"block-title\" itemprop=\"headline\">Penalty goal! Australia 36-20 Argentina (Hodge 75)</h2>\n<div class=\"block-elements block-elements--no-byline\" itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n<p>From 40m out he clears the crossbar with ease. </p>\n</div>\n\n<p class=\"block-share--liveblog-mobile\" data-open-overlay-on-click=\"share-modal-block-57dd2fdae4b0df02df203290\" data-link-name=\"open mobile block share\">\n<button class=\"block-share__item--mobile button button--small button--tertiary mobile-only\">\nShare\n</button>\n</p>\n\n</div>\n<div id=\"block-57dd2f57e4b0df02df20328f\" class=\"block block--content\" itemprop=\"liveBlogUpdate\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/BlogPosting\">\n<p class=\"block-time published-time\">\n<a href=\"/sport/live/2016/sep/17/rugby-championship-australia-v-argentina-live?page=with:block-57dd2f57e4b0df02df20328f#block-57dd2f57e4b0df02df20328f\" itemprop=\"url\" class=\"block-time__link\">\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T11:58:15.000Z\" data-relativeformat=\"med\" class=\" js-timestamp\" itemprop=\"datePublished\">9.58pm <span class=\"timezone\">AEST</span></time>\n<span class=\"block-time__absolute\">21:58</span>\n</a>\n</p>\n<div class=\"block-elements block-elements--no-byline\" itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n<p><strong>74 min:</strong> A penalty to Australia from 40m out from the Pumas\u2019 posts. That narrows the penalty count to 16-6 in Argentina\u2019s favour. </p>\n<p>Given the possibility of pushing Australia\u2019s lead out to beyond two converted tries Hodge will have a shot. </p>\n</div>\n\n<p class=\"block-share--liveblog-mobile\" data-open-overlay-on-click=\"share-modal-block-57dd2f57e4b0df02df20328f\" data-link-name=\"open mobile block share\">\n<button class=\"block-share__item--mobile button button--small button--tertiary mobile-only\">\nShare\n</button>\n</p>\n\n</div>\n<div id=\"block-57dd2f13e4b0c762d480d5eb\" class=\"block block--content is-key-event\" itemprop=\"liveBlogUpdate\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/BlogPosting\">\n<p class=\"block-time published-time\">\n<a href=\"/sport/live/2016/sep/17/rugby-championship-australia-v-argentina-live?page=with:block-57dd2f13e4b0c762d480d5eb#block-57dd2f13e4b0c762d480d5eb\" itemprop=\"url\" class=\"block-time__link\">\n<time datetime=\"2016-09-17T11:55:58.000Z\" data-relativeformat=\"med\" class=\" js-timestamp\" itemprop=\"datePublished\">9.55pm <span class=\"timezone\">AEST</span></time>\n<span class=\"block-time__absolute\">21:55</span>\n</a>\n</p>\n<h2 class=\"block-title\" itemprop=\"headline\">Conversion! {"timestamp": "1474092277000", "url": "https://www.theguardian.com/books/2016/sep/17/field-of-dreams-author-ends-his-life-under-assisted-dying-legislation", "author": "Associated Press", "title": "Field of Dreams book author ends his life under assisted-dying legislation", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/sport/blog/2013/sep/06/joy-of-six-fictional-sporting-film-characters\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Canadian novelist WP Kinsella</a>, who blended magical realism and baseball in the book <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/film/filmblog/2015/mar/26/the-film-that-makes-me-cry-field-of-dreams\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">that became the smash hit film Field of Dreams</a>, has died. He was 81.<br/></p>\n<p>His literary agent Carolyn Swayze said in a statement that Kinsella\u2019s death on Friday in Hope, British Columbia was doctor-assisted.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jun/06/canada-assisted-dying-suicide-law-deadline\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Assisted deaths became legal in Canada in June, 2016</a>.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-1 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__container\">\n<p class=\"rich-link__header\">\n<h1 class=\"rich-link__title\">Assisted dying to become legal in Canada but without clear guidelines</h1>\n</p>\n\n<a class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jun/06/canada-assisted-dying-suicide-law-deadline\"/>\n</div>\n</div>\n</aside>\n<p>In the 1982 novel Shoeless Joe, a farmer hears a voice telling him to build a baseball diamond in his corn fields. When he does, Shoeless Joe Jackson and other baseball players of yesteryear come to play. It became the blueprint for the 1989 Oscar-nominated movie, which starred <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/film/kevin-costner\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Kevin Costner</a>, James Earl Jones and Ray Liotta.</p>\n<p>Key turns of phrases in Kinsella\u2019s book \u201cIf you build it, they will come\u201d and \u201cGo the distance\u201d have taken their place in literature\u2019s lexicon and among Hollywood\u2019s most memorable movie lines.<br/></p>\n<p>Kinsella, a bona fide baseball junkie, loved the movie and said he had tears in his eyes when he first saw it.</p>\n<p>In 2011 the Canadian baseball Hall of Fame awarded him the Jack Graney Award for a significant contribution to the game of baseball in <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/canada\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">Canada</a>.<br/></p>\n<p>\u201cI wrote it 30 years ago, and the fact that people are still discovering it makes me proud. It looks like it will stand the test of time,\u201d Kinsella said at the time.</p>\n<p>Scott Crawford, director of operations at the Canadian hall, said he was saddened to learn of the author\u2019s death.</p>\n<p>\u201cHis work has touched the lives of thousands of baseball fans across Canada and around the world,\u201d Crawford said in a statement. \u201cHis most famous book was the classic Shoeless Joe, which inspired one of my favorite movies, Field of Dreams.\u201d</p>\n<p>Kinsella brought back to life Moonlight Graham, who played one major league baseball game but never got to bat. The author noticed Graham\u2019s name while thumbing through the Baseball Encyclopedia he had received as a Christmas gift from his father-in-law.</p>\n<p>\u201cI found this entry for Moonlight Graham. How could anyone come up with that nickname? He played one game but did not get to bat. I was intrigued, and I made a note that I intended to write something about him,\u201d Kinsella said in 2005 on the 100th anniversary of the only game Graham played in the majors.</p>\n<p>Much of Kinsella\u2019s work touched on baseball. He published almost 30 books of fiction, non-fiction and poetry and won the Order of Canada, one of the country\u2019s highest honors.</p>\n<p>William Patrick Kinsella was born in Edmonton, Alberta. His father John had played minor league baseball, and the young Kinsella fell for the game playing with friends on sandlots in Edmonton.</p>\n<p>He began writing as a child, winning a YMCA contest at age 14.</p>\n<p>Kinsella took writing courses at the University of Victoria in 1970, receiving his bachelor of arts in creative writing in 1974. In 1978 he earned a master of fine arts in English through the Iowa Writers\u2019 Workshop at the University of Iowa.</p>\n<p>He had been an English professor at the University of Calgary.</p>\n<p>Vancouver Writer\u2019s Festival founder Alma Lee said Kinsella was a private man with a passion for baseball.</p>\n<p>\u201cHe was a dedicated story-teller, performer, curmudgeon, an irascible and difficult man,\u201d Swayze said in a statement. \u201cHis fiction has made people laugh, cry, and think for decades and will do so for decades to come.\u201d</p>\n<p>Kinsella was married three times. He is survived by two daughters, who the literary agency says cared for him in his final years, and several grandchildren.<br/></p>\n<p>Kinsella has asked there be no memorial service.</p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "summary": "WP Kinsella\u2019s book Shoeless Joe was turned into the huge hit film Field Of Dreams in 1989"}

modelling shows Great Australian Bight oil spill could reach NSW", "content": "<html><body><div><div class=\"content__article-body from-content-api js-article__body\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" data-test-id=\"article-review-body\">\n<p>An uncontrolled oil spill from BP\u2019s planned wells in the Great Australian Bight could affect the coastline as far away as New South Wales, according to previously secret oil-spill modelling uploaded to the company\u2019s website this week.</p>\n<p>Within 24 hours of the modelling being uploaded to BP\u2019s website, the regulator, the National Offshore Petroleum Safety and Environmental Management Authority (Nopsema) announced it would take a further 10 days to assess BP\u2019s plans to drill in the area.</p>\n<p>Nopsema\u2019s assessment of BP\u2019s environmental plan would now be completed on 29 September, it said on Friday.</p>\n<p>In 2015, frustrated by a lack of published modelling, the Wilderness Society had commissioned its own modelling, which suggested a spill would have a major impact on most of the southern coast of Australia and Tasmania.</p>\n<p>But the summary of official <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/bp\" data-link-name=\"auto-linked-tag\" data-component=\"auto-linked-tag\" class=\"u-underline\">BP</a> modelling showing what it considers a worst-case scenario appears to suggest a much more severe impact over a much larger area.</p>\n<figure class=\"element element-interactive interactive\" data-interactive=\"https://interactive.guim.co.uk/embed/iframe-wrapper/0.1/boot.js\" data-canonical-url=\"https://interactive.guim.co.uk/charts/embed/sep/2016-09-16T04:14:01/embed.html\" data-alt=\"Oil spill impact on coastline\">\n<a href=\"https://interactive.guim.co.uk/charts/embed/sep/2016-09-16T04:14:01/embed.html\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Oil spill impact on coastline</a>\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img\">\nChance coastal locations will be affected by a moderate oil spill in the Great Australian Bight\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>According to BP\u2019s results, the NSW coast would have a 41% chance of being hit with \u201cmoderate shoreline contact\u201d<strong> </strong>within as little as 48 days of a<strong> </strong>spill in winter months.</p>\n<p>In some months, Adelaide would have a 97% chance of being hit with the same sort of contact, possibly within 36 days.</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail element-rich-link--not-upgraded\" data-component=\"rich-link\" data-link-name=\"rich-link-1 | 1\">\n<div class=\"rich-link\">\n<div class=\"rich-link__link u-faux-block-link__overlay\" having a 100% chance of moderate shoreline contact in some months, including Port Lincoln, Kangaroo Island and the area between Elliston and Coffin Bay.</p>\n<p>BP has said it could completely cap blow-out within 35 days, but its modelling reveals many coastal areas could be hit before that happened.</p>\n<p>A spokeswoman for BP told Guardian Australia: \u201cAs part of our commitment to transparency, we have made these results available publicly.</p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s important to remember that the modelling assumes that a worst credible discharge has taken place with no measures designed to prevent this from happening being considered. It also assumes that no attempts to control, contain, disperse or recover the oil are attempted \u2013 whereas in reality all these measures would be employed,\u201d she said.</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  \" data-media-id=\"ab4fa2e2273588c5fbb972fdb2834011ee64adf3\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/uploads/2016/09/16/oilspill3.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=212d697ea8d88e7eac4ed33feb835661\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"620\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"411\"/>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nPhotograph: Guardian\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>\u201cWe will be able to move oil spill response equipment anywhere in that area within two days.\u201d</p>\n<p>Wilderness Society campaigner Peter Owen told Guardian Australia the modelling justified the concerns the organisation had been raising.</p>\n<p>\u201cIt took 87 days to cap a blow-out in the Gulf of Mexico, which is one of the most developed oil fields in the world,\u201d Owen said. \u201cThere\u2019s nothing nearby in the Great Australian Bight.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cModerate shoreline contact\u201d means water with 100 grams per square metre of oil on it. That is 10 times the amount needed for a \u201cmetallic sheen\u201d to be visible on the water. BP says when there is a metallic sheen there would already be mortality among seabirds and other marine wildlife.</p>\n<p>That level of spill would move further than the areas likely to be affected by \u201cmoderate shoreline contact\u201d and would affect fisheries. In the US, fisheries shut down with a concentration of just 0.01 grams per square metre.<br/></p>\n<p>A spokesman for the Wilderness Society said: \u201cBP\u2019s latest spill modelling summary also finally admits to the unacceptable impact that a spill in the Bight could have on critically important ecological systems and marine species that Australia has clear international obligations to protect.\u201d</p>\n<p>This week <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2016/sep/12/call-to-halt-great-australian-bight-oil-drilling-amid-faulty-equipment-fears\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\"> the Guardian revealed</a> that BP could drill in the Great Australian Bight using potentially faulty equipment, which the US regulator has said could cause a major disaster.</p>\n<p>A leading international expert on oil disasters, Bob Bea, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2016/sep/16/oil-disaster-investigator-alarmed-by-bp-great-australian-bight-response\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">said BP\u2019s response</a> to the concerns was totally inadequate, and an \u201cearly warning sign\u201d of problems that could lead to a disaster.</p>\n<p>On Thursday the <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2016/sep/15/senate-reopens-inquiry-into-plans-to-drill-in-great-australian-bight\" data-link-name=\"in body link\" class=\"u-underline\">Senate agreed</a> to launch fresh scrutiny of BP\u2019s plans, with two public hearings.</p>\n<p>BP has been contacted for comment.</p>\n</div>\n</div></body></html>", "summary": "Company\u2019s model shows a spill from its proposed well could have a much more devastating effect on coasts and marine life than previously thought"}

He is a father of two young children and a popular, talented sportsman who excels at rugby and golf. If you got to know him well, you might discover a few quirks. He doesn\u2019t permit any black in his house. There won\u2019t ever be a leather sofa in his living room. He will never stock up on Jaffa Cakes for his kitchen cupboard. And he won\u2019t allow his four-year-old son to have a bunk bed.</p>\n<p>His partner, Emily, discovered the reason when she found him curled in a ball by their spare bed, a sweating \u201cgibbering wreck\u201d after they argued one day six years ago: \u201cI can still see him there, cowering, a big man, trying to get under the bed. He was like a little boy, whimpering, not lucid, as if he was in a flashback. I managed to get him on to the bed and held him, which normally he doesn\u2019t let me do. That was a pivotal moment, seeing what was going on in his head.\u201d</p>\n<p>In the first year of their relationship, James hinted that he\u2019d had a horrible time at school. Emily wasn\u2019t given the whole story at once but, gradually, the secret that he\u2019d kept close for more than 30 years came out: the physical and sexual abuse he\u2019d suffered when he was nine years old.</p>\n<p>In 1980, James\u2019s parents, a businessman and a teacher, decided that their eldest son would benefit from a private education at a boarding school in Suffolk. St George\u2019s was an impressive-looking former stately home with a sweeping drive. On his first night, he and other homesick boys were hauled out of their metal bunk-beds by two prefects. Wearing slippers, a dressing gown and starchy new pyjamas, James was led along corridors until he came to a black door beneath a winding staircase. They could hear\u00a0crying.</p>\n<p>Inside was a long leather sofa, a big desk on which lay a cane and a contraption that resembled an oversized table-tennis bat and two men: Derek Slade, the headmaster, and Gerard Singer, the head of languages. James does not like to call them by their names. For him, it dignifies them. \u201cI built up such a resilience to them. I\u2019d prefer \u2018him\u2019 to be \u2018it\u2019,\u201d he says.</p>\n<p>James was ordered to turn around and drop his trousers. Then he was whacked with \u201csix of the best\u201d. After a few weeks and more beatings \u2013 \u201cyou\u2019re punished for crying, you\u2019re punished for not having your shoes polished, it was all very regimented\u201d \u2013 James was summoned again to the room with the black door. There, waiting, were the same two teachers.</p>\n<p>\u201cI knocked on the black door and walked into the room and Slade was behind his desk. My normal thing was to go and adopt my position and drop my trousers, and I stood there waiting. I didn\u2019t take much notice but his trousers were round his ankles. I was waiting for the cane and he came over and thrust his penis into me and that was the first time he raped me.\u201d</p>\n<aside class=\"element element-pullquote element--supporting\">\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n<blockquote>\n<p class=\"pullquote-paragraph\">My relationships haven\u2019t been intimate or cuddly. I look at other couples and it tortures me that I\u2019m unable to do that</p>\n</blockquote>\n<span class=\"inline-quote inline-icon closing inline-tone-fill\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 33 20\" class=\"closing__svg inline-tone-fill__svg inline-quote__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M9.002 20c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553C4.065 2.97 7.415.937 11.004 1l-1-1C3.98 0 .098 4.447.003 10.006c-.098 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994zm17 0c3.85.068 6.932-3.104 7-6.994.068-3.892-3.15-6.937-7-7.006-2.016-.036-3.59.694-4.888 2.053-.07-.48-.122-1.04-.113-1.553.064-3.53 3.414-5.563 7.003-5.5l-1-1c-6.022 0-9.904 4.447-10 10.006-.097 5.557 3.35 9.892 9 9.994z\"/>\n</svg> </span>\n</aside>\n<p>James uses such unequivocal language now because, in the witness box of Ipswich crown court, where Singer finally stood trial earlier this summer, James was told by the judge that he had to speak more plainly. \u201cSeveral times, the judge said, \u2018You have to say what he is doing.\u2019 In court, you have to be graphic and say \u2018penis\u2019 and \u2018penis inside you\u2019 and \u2018semen\u2019.\u201d</p>\n<p>That was a shock to James: he hadn\u2019t been warned in advance by the Crown Prosecution Service, for whom he was a key witness.</p>\n<p>After the abuse, James was sent back to his dorm. \u201cAs you walk out of the door, there was a table with Jaffa Cakes. They said, \u2018Take three Jaffa Cakes\u2019. When you\u2019re away from home and the school meals are absolutely awful, a Jaffa Cake was like Willy Wonka\u2019s Golden Ticket.\u201d</p>\n<p>James was raped between 25 and 30 times by both teachers in a year, before they abruptly left the school without explanation. \u201cYou go home at Christmas just a broken child. I just can\u2019t get excited by Christmas now. All these things have triggers in later life.\u201d</p>\n<p>After they fell in love, Emily became used to James\u2019s reluctance to be tactile. Their first house had a galley kitchen. \u201cYou just can\u2019t share that space. It\u2019s like a forcefield around him. He will flinch if I go to touch him,\u201d she says. \u201cJames is not in any way violent or physically abusive. I\u2019ve never feared that he would be to any of us, but there is a swirling vortex of negative energy around him. It comes into the room with him and it\u2019s bigger than him.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cMy relationships haven\u2019t been intimate or cuddly, I don\u2019t do all that,\u201d says James. \u201cHolding hands, touching someone\u2019s shoulder at a party, which is normal in normal relationships, is not normal for me. I look at other couples and it tortures me that I\u2019m not able to do that.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cIt also tortures me to see the closeness between other couples,\u201d adds Emily. \u201cI desperately want it too. Living like this is very lonely.\u201d</p>\n<p>Around the time Emily came to understand his past, James discovered several old schoolmates on Facebook discussing the arrest of their former headmaster, Derek Slade. \u201cI was really struggling with life. I was near Ipswich, where the trial was, and went into the public gallery. I saw this shrivelled old man with a big Santa Claus beard in the dock. I looked at him and he looked at me. It put the fear of God into me. I just got up and walked out.\u201d</p>\n<figure itemprop=\"associatedMedia image\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" data-component=\"image\" class=\"element element-image img--landscape  fig--narrow-caption fig--has-shares \" data-media-id=\"63ec5a619e78d806d37ab69bad907edc0e5cc694\" id=\"img-2\">\n<meta itemprop=\"url\" content=\"https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/63ec5a619e78d806d37ab69bad907edc0e5cc694/0_0_5574_3344/5574.jpg?w=700&amp;q=55&amp;auto=format&amp;usm=12&amp;fit=max&amp;s=63b0492874d4031a93257ae8bf9f3c3b\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"5574\"/>\n<meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"3344\"/>\n<a href=\"#img-2\" class=\"article__img-container js-gallerythumbs\" data-link-name=\"Launch Article Lightbox\" data-is-ajax=\"\">\n <span class=\"inline-expand-image inline-icon centered-icon rounded-icon article__fullscreen modern-visible\">\n<svg viewbox=\"0 0 22 22\" class=\"centered-icon__svg rounded-icon__svg article__fullscreen__svg modern-visible__svg inline-expand-image__svg inline-icon__svg\">\n<path d=\"M3.4 20.2L9 14.5 7.5 13l-5.7 5.6L1 14H0v7.5l.5.5H8v-1l-4.6-.8M18.7 1.9L13 7.6 14.4 9l5.7-5.7.5 4.7h1.2V.6l-.5-.5H14v1.2l4.7.6\"/>\n</svg> </span> </a>\n\n<figcaption class=\"caption caption--img caption caption--img\" itemprop=\"description\">\nGiving evidence in court was harrowing for James but afterwards, \u2018the weight went from my shoulders,\u2019 he says. Photograph: Posed by model/Getty Images\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p>Slade\u2019s conviction \u2013 jailed for 21 years \u2013 \u201ctriggered something\u201d in James, and he resolved to do something about his second abuser, Gerard Singer.</p>\n<p>He went to the police and spent hours giving evidence and undergoing medical examinations (doctors\u2019 evidence formed part of the prosecution against Singer). Although Emily knew about his childhood trauma, James was still reluctant to share the progress of his case, which took six years to come to trial. He was upset when a new police liaison officer casually asked him what his case was about (she hadn\u2019t bothered to check) and when he was told there wasn\u2019t time to visit the court before the trial to familiarise himself with the surroundings. \u201cI felt I was always chasing the police,\u201d he says. \u201cI was expecting a bit more support. Since the trial, I\u2019ve heard nothing from them.\u201d</p>\n<p>\u201cQuite often things would be terrible between us and only afterwards it would transpire that something had happened with the police or the court case,\u201d says Emily. \u201cI\u2019ve tried many times to ask him about his experiences. On the one hand, I have to be sensitive and not pry. On the other, I\u2019ve been pushed away quite venomously so many times, I\u2019m reluctant to put myself there. He keeps himself this closed book. I\u2019m a very open person but in order to preserve my own sanity I\u2019ve had to emotionally turn away.\u201d</p>\n<p>In this way, the abuse \u201cdoesn\u2019t stop when it stopped 35 years ago\u201d, says Emily. \u201cThe evil is still within our family because it has its impact on him and his behaviour and we\u2019re living with that every day.\u201d</p>\n<p>James, she says, is \u201cquite reluctant\u201d to seek help. At first, they tried couples counselling but Emily says it didn\u2019t really work. She believes he needs specialist counselling. \u201cIt takes him a long time to build up trust in the counsellor,\u201d she says.</p>\n<p>Giving evidence against his abuser in court was \u201cthe most harrowing thing I\u2019ve had to do in my life,\u201d says James. \u201cIt could go two ways. You could be believed or you could be back in there for contempt of court.\u201d</p>\n<p>On the day he was called to give evidence, their four-year-old son, Billy, could tell he was upset.</p>\n<p>James and Emily told him that Daddy had to sort out some problems at work. He\u2019s there to protect you.\u201d</p>\n<p>James put Captain Barnacles \u2013 the leader of the Octonauts cartoon \u2013 in his pocket when he stood in the witness box. \u201cWhen it was getting harrowing, I pulled him out and just broke down. Most importantly, James \u2013 and eight other abused former pupils who gave evidence \u2013 was believed. Singer was found guilty of all 27 counts of abuse. He was sentenced to 21 years in prison and a further eight on licence.</p>\n<p>\u201cI\u2019ve suffered torment of a great magnitude. The physical side of things is never going to heal,\u201d says James. \u201cWhen a child comes to you, stop and listen. We can never eradicate evil but we can always listen.\u201d</p>\n<p>After the trial, they went on holiday and Emily caught a \u201cglimpse\u201d of a happier future for their family. \u201cJames was open and communicative and perceptive and he understood how we could have a normal conversation about things and the life going on around him. I\u2019d been living with this block of stone for four years and now he was starting to show some emotion. You don\u2019t want to see someone hurting but it\u2019s preferable to them blocking it out and taking it out on everyone around them.\u201d</p>\n<p>However, \u201cThat kind of closed again,\u201d says Emily. \u201cI never expected everything to be instantly better. We had this amazing breakthrough. It was impossible for that to last because it can\u2019t be that easy [to get over abuse].\u201d</p>\n<p>Emily worries about the impact of a \u201ctoxic atmosphere\u201d on their children. \u201cI want the home to be a place of sanctuary for the children, not stress. This is the point at which things have to start moving forward or else he is never going to change. He needs to see what he has to lose. Do you want that terrible thing that happened in the past to ruin your future? Don\u2019t let those people ruin any more of your life.\u201d</p>\n<p>What of his parents, who sent him to the school in the first place?</p>\n<p>Ten years ago, when James\u2019s parents bailed him out of a serious debt, his mother asked him what was wrong and he finally told her about the abuse. He says he and his father don\u2019t have a very close bond but doesn\u2019t blame his parents for sending him away and shows me an email from his father, expressing his love, support and admiration for his son. \u201cThey did what they thought was best. She\u2019s never seen that part of me and I\u2019ve never seen that part of me. I want to put all of this dark stuff in a box.
